Of Hipocrisie.As concerning Hipocrisie: let him consider, if he haue laboured to seeme to be that which he is not, or haue fained himselfe to be more holie than he is indeed, to procure vainelie vnto him selfe the name and estimation of holines amongst men.
Of braging and boasting.Concerning bragging, vaunting, and boasting, let him consider, if hee haue after a vaine
 manner vaunted or praised himselfe, or his owne doinges.
If he haue praised himselfe for any sin he hath committed: as for that he hath dishonoured any woman, or done any iniurie vnto others.
If he haue co^mended himself for a thing which he neuer did, (especially being a sin,) that therby he might seeme a valiant and hardie man, or be the more esteemed.


II. OF COVETOVSNES.
LET him consider, if he haue bin couetous,Of Couetousnes. and nigardlie, or if he haue hoorded vp goods together without a reasonable cause.
If contrariwise he haue bin prodigal, and wasteful.
If hee haue spent more than his abilitie was able to maintaine,Of Prodigalitie. whereby hee is fallen into great necessity, and wa^teth meanes to prouide thinges necessarie for his wife, children, and seruants.
If he haue had a great and inordinate loue towardes money, whereby he hath forgotten almighty God, and such thinges as be requisite for the behoofe of his soule, and hath imployed his whole studie to the increasing of his worldly substance.
If he haue desired another mans death to be his heire, or executor, or to enioy some office, or other co^modity, after his death.
3. Of Leacherie: Of this sinne we haue treated alreadie in the Sixt Commandement.



IIII. OF ANGER.
AS touching Anger: Let him consider first, if he haue bin so angrie with himselfe,Of Anger towardes himselfe. as to wish or desire his owne death.
If being in any rage or furie, hee haue hurt himselfe.
If in his anger he haue giuen himselfe to the Diuell, or cursed himselfe.
Of Anger towardes his neighbour.As touching his Neighbour: If he haue bin angrie with his Neighbour, or disdained him without cause.
If he haue spoken any wordes of anger against him, or giuen him discurteous language.
If hee haue reuiled him with iniurious wordes: as calling him theefe, drunkard, or foole, etc. not being his seruant, or bondman. This is a deadly sinne.
If in his choller and anger hee haue vpbraided him with his faults, and offences, which he hath committed, therby to make him ashamed.
If he haue in his anger vttered the same words, or discouered vnto others the same faults in his neighbours absence.
If hee haue cursed or offered vnto the diuel the creatures of God, or wished vengeance vpon them, whether they were his
 seruants or not: though there be some difference betweene the one offence, and the other.
If he haue beene obstinate, chollericke, wayward, or quarrelling: or haue vsed any vnciuile tearmes in his wordes, and reasonings.
If hee haue executed the anger of his minde against any man, by striking him.


V. OF GLVTTONIE.
AS touching gluttonie: let him consider, if he haue broken any of the Fasting dayes prescribed by the Catholicke Church.
If hee haue eaten flesh vppon any daie prohibited without sufficient cause.
If he haue bin occasion that any other hath broken anye Fasting daye, which they were bound to keepe. This also is a deadly sinne.
If he haue eaten so excessiuely, or such meates, as were hurtfull vnto his health.
If he haue eaten or drunken ouermuch, or oftentimes, or with ouermuch appetite, or gluttonous desire.
If hee haue beene a great louer of such meates as are delicate, and curiouslie dressed,
 and haue bestowed very much therevpon.
Against dronkennes. Prouer. 20. vers. 1. Prou. 31.4. Eccles. ^9.2. Eccles. 51.38. Esaie. 5.11. Osee. 4.^1. Ioel 1.5. Luc. 21. vers. ^4. Rom. 13.^3. 1. Cor. 5.^0. Galath. 5.21. Ephes. ^.18. Concil Magunt. Can ^6.If hee haue willinglie made himselfe druncke, or any other, it is a deadlie sinne.
Here let such take heed, as vse that abhominable drunken custome of Germany, lately come vp, and practised now in many places of England, to carouse and drinke vnmea urably one to another. The which beastlie sinne of drunkennesse (being a voluntary madnes,) is also an occasion of many other deadlie sinnes, that doe consequently follow the same. In consideration whereof, it was ordeined by an auncient Councell, that who so is oftentimes drunken and will not amend, after that he is reprehended for it, should be excommunicated.


VI. OF ENVIE.
^f Enuie.AS touching Enuie: let him consider, if hee haue with a deliberate aduise bin grieued at the prosperitie of others, or because others excelled him in any thing. As if a Courtier should enuie that another should be in greater credit, or fauour than he, or be better preferred, or obteine his suites with more expedition.
If hee haue reioyced at his Neighbours hurt, or aduersitie, or to see him fallen from his wonted credit, and estimation.
If hee haue spoken euill wordes of his neighbour to discredit his person, or his good name, and fame, or to aduance himself,
 by disclosing the faults and defects of others
If he haue discouered any secret fault of his neighbour, to the end, that his defectes being published his credit might be diminished.
If it hath grieued him, when he heard his neighbour well reported of.


VII. OF SLOVTH.
AS touching Slouth:Of Slouth. let him consider, if for slouthfulnesse he haue omitted to doe good workes: as to heare Masse, to say his prayers, especially, when of dutie he is bound vnto them.
If in his praiers, and other good exercises appertaining vnto the seruice of Almighty god, he hath done the same coldly or faintly, and after a light and negligent sort.
If he haue beene inconstant,Of Inconstancy. giuing ouer such good purposes as he intended to do, and leauing of his deuotions, and other holy Exercises, vpon euery light occasion.
If he haue deferred the^ from day to day.
If he haue slept more than is necessarie.
If he haue spent his time lewdlie in vaine fantasticall and wandring thoughts, in idle talke, and vnfruitfull exercises.
If in his troubles and aduersities he haue taken ouermuch griefe thereof.
If on the contrarie part hee haue waxen
 proud, and haughtie aboue measure, with prosperitie, estimation, and good successe, not giuing the glorie therof vnto almightie God.



Of the workes of mercy.
Of spirituall workes of mercie.AS concerning the Workes of Mercy: let him first accuse himselfe, if hee haue beene negligent in the spirituall workes of mercie: especially if hee haue omitted to counsaile, aduise, or reprehend such persons, as hee might haue holpen by some of these meanes, chieflie if they were such, as of dutie he was bound to haue care of.
If when he hath eyther counsailed, or reprehended them, he did it in such anger, and with so little modestie, that hee did more harme than good.
^f brotherly ^^rrection. ^^cle. 17. ^^rse. 12. ^^t. 22.39. ^ath. 18. ^^r. 15.16.17 ^^mma. S. ^^omae. 22. ^est. 33. ar. ^. and 3. and ^^od lib. 11. ^^e^. 10. arti. (...) 13. and ^e Sum^^lam.Note, that the precept of brotherly correction, is a precept of charity, and spirituall almes, and is therefore called a brotherly correction, or admonition, because it tendeth to amend our brother of his sin in a charitable manner: and the order thou must vse herein, is prescribed in the ghospell, to wit. First to admonish thy brother secretly of his sin. Secondly, if he amend not, then to take with thee one or two witnesses. Thirdly, if that notwithstanding hee amend not, then to declare it to the Church: to wit, to the Prelates, or Gouernours of the Church, as S. Chrisostome interpreteth it: But note, that so long as thou hast any probable hope of amending thy brother by secret admonition of him, thou must vse it
 more ofte^ than once,Caietani, de peccatis. tit Correctio Fratterna. and Paulum de Palacio in Math. cap 18. and Stellam in Luc. cap. 17. Et Nauarr. i^ Manuali Confessario Cap. 24. Numer. 12.13.14. and cap 18. Num. 56 Proue. 24.1 Eccle. 11.7. Iac. 3.2. Prou. 24.1^ 1-Tim-5.2^ Prouerb. 9. vers. 7.8. Prou. 15.1^ Prou. 17.1 Prou. 29.2 Eccle. 1.1 Eccle. 3. Eccle. 20. Prou. 31.4 2. Thes. 5.1 Psa. 140.5 1. Cor. 4.1 Gal. 6.1. 1. Tim. 5.1 2. Tim. 2.2 for preseruing his good name and fame: Because wheras the sinner incurreth two euils by his sinne, the one is hurt of his conscience, and the other is hurt of his fame, if thou canst repaire the hurt of his conscience without hurting his fame thou oughtest so to doe: But in case thy secret admonition doth not preuaile with him, then sith the hurt of his conscience is the greater euill, the same ought to be preferred, and holpen, although it be with the hurt of his fame. But note also first, that thou must not vse this brotherly correction, or admonition vnto any, vnlesse thou be verie certaine, that they are guiltie, and thou art not bou^d to vse it, when thou haste but a suspition therof, albeit it be with coniectures. Secondlie note, that the sinne of thy brother which is to be thus brotherlie corrected, must be a sinne, whereby he is in danger to perish, I meane a deadly sinne: for in veniall sinnes, (as S. Iames saith) vve doe all offend. Thirdly note, that a publike sinner is publikelie to be corrected, and reprehended for his sinne, as S. Paule affirmeth. Fourthly note, that thou art not bound to correct the sins of such persons, as thou haste no hope that they will be reformed and amended thereby: as the sinnes of such vvith vvhome thou haste no conuersation: for it is likely, that they vvill giue no eare vnto thee. Neyther yet art thou bound to correct or admonish such persons of their sins, as in thy opinion are carefull of their consciences, and be therefore likely to repent and amend of themselues. Fiftly note, that thou must seeke good opportunitie of time and place to vse this brotherly correction. and in any wise to admonish him charitably as thy brother, and not as an enimie: otherwise doing it vvithout discretion, thou shalt doe more hurt than good.

Sixtly note, that if another hauing knowledge of that sinne be more apt and likely to admonish him of the same sinne, than thou art, and is disposed therunto, thou maiest then omit this brotherly correction, and admonition.
If he haue not had compassion of so many miseries, calamities, rebellions, sects, and heresies, as do at this day trouble all Christendome: And if he haue not praied vnto Almighty God for redresse of them.
^f Corporal ^orkes of ^ercie.As touching the corporall works of mercie: let him consider, if he haue holpen his Neighbours in their troubles, and necessities. And if hee haue giuen Almes to the poore, according to his abilitie.
If he haue bin cholericke with them, or murmured against them, or giuen them euill answeres, as being too much molested by their importunitie: or if he haue disdained, or mocked them.


Of other Accusations more particular.
AFTER these Accusations, which are common to all kind of persons, there be other speciall Accusations, which apperteine vnto diuers kindes of States, or persons: as to Bishops, Curats, Priests, Religious Munkes, Friers, and Nuns, Lawiers, Iudges, Sergeants, Counsailers, Officers, Atturneys, Proctors, witnesses, Iurors, gouernours of Cities, Stewards of copy holds,
 or other segniories, Phisitions, Marchants, House-houlders, or such like: the which kinds of persons ought to accuse themselues, after these general accusations, of such matters also, as do appertaine particularly vnto the charge of their estates, and Offices.
The Prelates, (to vvit Bishops,Bishops and Curates. Pastours, and Curates) that haue charge of soules, ought to accuse themselues, if they haue not bene resident, and of the little regard and care, they haue had to instruct and profit their flocke, with Catholicke doctrine, prayers, and good example of life.
See the godly decrees in the late holy Generall Councell of Trent,Concilium Generale Trident. Sess. 5. de Reformatione. cap. 2. and Sess. 24. de Reformatione. Cap. 4. Concil. Generale Lateran. Can. 10. how all Curates are bound to preach themselues, or hauing lawfull impediment to cause others that are meete for the same to preach the word of God to their flocke, at the least all Sondaies, and Solemne Festiuall dayes. And note there also, hovv all Bishoppes are bound to preach them elues, or hauing lawfull impediment to appoint other meete Preachers, to Preach the word of God to the people in their Diocesse, at the least all Sondaies, and Solemne Festiuall dayes, and in the Holy times of Lent, and Aduent euery day: or at the least three dayes euery vveeke. And see the like Decree ordeined in auncient time, in the Holy Generall Councell of Lateran, holden vnder Pope Innocentius the third.
The Priests,Priests. if they haue not said Masse, and other diuine seruice: or haue saide the same negligently, with little reuerence, attention, and deuotion.
The religious persons:Religious persons. if they haue broken
 any of their vowes, or any ordinaunces of their Order.
Note, that by the late Holy generall Councell of Trent,Conc. gener. Trid. Sess. 25 cap 18. de regular. and Monial. al such are excommunicated, as doe by any meanes enforce any virgin, or other woman, against their wils to enter into any Monastery, or to put on the habit of a Religious Nunne, or to be professed.
And likewise all such are excommunicated by the saide Generall Councell, as doe by any meanes hinder without iust cause, the Holy will of any Virgin, or other Woman, from being a Religious Nunne, or from making any vowe for the same.
Sebast. Med. in summa peccat. part 2. pag. 253. Concil. Trid. Sess. 25. cap. 5. de regular. and Monial libNote also, that if any doe enter without necessary cause within the inclosure of Nunnes, albeit it be done vnder pretence of licence graunted by the Ordinarie, and not reuoked, they be Excommunicated. Greg. 13. Extr. de anno. 1575. anno 4. And the Abbesses and Nunnes are likewise Excommunicated by the same Decree, that permitte them to enter. And note, that by the Councell of Trent, the licence of the Bishop or Superior for the same must be obtained in writing: which they may not graunt, but onlie in necessary cases.
The Iudge^:Iudges. If for any worldly respect, as friendshippe, hatred, kindred, feare, subornation, or bribery, they haue not ministred Iustice syncerely, and rightly, or haue prolonged the same, without cause.
The Laweirs,Lawiers. as Sergeants, Counsailours, Officers, Attourneis, solicitours, or Proctours, if for want of sufficient learning, or in other respectes, they be vnmeet to discharge their duties: or if they haue deceiued their clients, by fauoring publickely or secretly their aduersaries: or haue willingly lost or hindered the iust and rightfull cause of the
 the other aduersarie, by vouching false lawes, knowing them to be false, or by friuolous argume^ts cauills, and reasonings, to obscure the same, or by procuring superfluous delaies.
If they haue not bene ^arefull to examin whether their Clientes cause were iust or no.
If they haue gone forewardes, and prosequuted their Clientes vniust cause, knowing it to be vniust, yea, and though at the beginning of the suite they know it not to be vniust, but afterwards whe^ it appeared vnto the^ to be so, if they did then defend the same, it is to be confessed as a deadly sin. For albeit they ought not to discouer the iniustice,Manuale Confessariorum Nauarr. cap. 25. numer. 28. of their Clientes causes to their aduersaries, yet are they bound to giue ouer the defence of them, and to declare to their clientes their opinion therin, and to endeuour to perswade them vnto an honest agreement.
If they haue concealed from their clientes, and not vttered to them the vniustice, and naughtines of their causes.
If they haue taught their clientes to lie, or to vse deceites, and vniust meanes, against their aduersaries: as to bribe the Iudge or vndersherife: to procure the impanell to be made at their particular denomination: to corrupt any of the Iury. to counterfeit false writings: to bring false witnesses, or such like.
If they haue not holpen whe^ they might the iust causes of the poore, being in extreme necessitie:Summa. S. Thom. 22. quest. 71. artic. 1. and. Manuale Confess. Nauarr. cap. 25. numer. 29. I meane, at what time the poore mans life, or vtter vndoing depended vpon the defence of his iust cause, and he wanted helpe therein.
If they haue taken litle care for their Clientes causes, and haue not studied to giue them their best counsail: or if by their default their clients, haue
 taken any preiudice or domage in their causes.
If they haue taken vpon them moe matters than they were well able to dispatch.
A good note for Atturnies.If they haue labour^d, procured, or consented, to prolong and delay their Clients suites contrary to the due order of iustice: or haue not endeuoured to bring them quicklie to an end.
If they haue taken too great fees of their Clients: or haue deceaued them in the accompts of their charges.
If when their clients were willing to fall to agreement, they haue hindered the same or haue perswaded them to continue still in sutes of law.
The Plaintifes if they haue made any vniust demaund, or sought only in their sinnes to vexe and molest the defendante with arestes, sub pena, latitat outlarie, citation: or haue endeuoured by any meanes to delaie their own sutes against iustice: or haue concealed or rent the writings, and euidences, which might disclose the truth of the whol matter. And let both the plaintiffesPlaintiffes. And defendantes accuse them selues, if in the suites betwene them they haue sought contentions, and quarells, or haue refrained to speake one to an other: or if they haue endeuoured to corrupt any of the Iudges,Manu. Conf. Nauarr. cap. 25. num. 31. Sebastianus. Medices, in Summa pec. par. 2 q 40. num. 38. officers, witnesses or Iurors, with letters, Bribes, Fauours, promisses, threatninges, or adherentes. And note, that who so accuseth an other of a false crime, or sueth an other, knowing that his ^ute in law is vniust, is bound to make restitution vnto the other for al his losses, and expenses, susteined thereby.
The witnesses:Witnesses. if vpon their othes they haue not testified the very truth sincerely, and plainly, and that without any deceit, fauour, enmity, feare or slander.Siluester. Tit. Testis. numer. 10. And note, that he that giueth false witnes, is bound to make restitution of al such losses as eyther the plaintiffes
 plaintiffes or defendants haue susteined by meanes of his false witnes giuen. And note also,Manuale co^fessariorum. Nauarr. Cap. 25. num. 45. Soto, de iustitia. and iure. lib. 5. quest 8. artic. 4. that if a witnesse take any rewarde to testifie the truth, he not only sinneth, but is also bou^d to make restitution thereof to him that gaue it him. Howbeit, he may take the expenses of his iournie, and recompence for all his losses susteined thereby. But Iurors in Enquestes cannot require any recompence for their expenses or losses thereby, because they are bound by the tenor of their freehold to serue their prince: and countrey (as it were iudges of the fact) therein.
The Phisitians:Phisitians. let them accuse them-selues: first,Siluester. tit. Medicus numer. 1. Sebastianus medices in Summa peccatorum. part. 2. quest. 39 in littera. M. num. 53. fol. 117 Manuale Confessariorum. Nauarr. Cap. 25 numer. 60.61.62.63.64. if they prescribe medicines without suff^cient knowledge in phisicke, though the Phisitian haue taken the degree of a Doctour of phisick Secondlie: if they follow not the precept^ of phisicke, vnlesse it be in some diseases which they can cure by long experience: howbeit they must not vse anie maner of inchauntment, or witch-crafte therein. Thirdly: if they neglect to studie, or to visite their patientes in their need. Fourthly: if they Presume to prescribe medicines for a disease before they knowe the disease. Fiftly: if when they dout of some medicine whether it will cure a disease they doe notwithstanding giue it to their patient, either to trie an experience, or to gaine thereby, or not to seeme to be ignorant in Phisicke. Sixthlie: if they giue to their patients such things as they know wil hurt the^, albeit they do earnestly request it. Seuenthly: if they forsake their patientes before they ought, that they either dye, or their sicknes is prolo^ged. Eightly if in da^gerous sicknes or diseases they cou^sel not their patie^ts to confesse their sins to their gostly father before they apply any medicines vnto the^, according as they be commaunded by the
 Holie Generall Councell of Lateran.Council. Generale Lateran. Canon. 23.Sebastianus Medices, in Summa peccatorum. part. 2. pag. 118. And note, that a Solemne Ecclesiasticall ordinance was published anno Domini. 1566. whereby al phisitians are straitlie prohibited to visit their patientes three daies together, vnlesse they haue before confessed their sinnes to their Ghostly Father. And in ca^e the Phisitians doe visitt them contrary thereunto they commit a deadly sinne, besides incurring diuerse other penalties pre^cribed in the said Ecclesiasticall ordinance. Ninthlie: if they prescribe or giue any thing to a woman with childe to destroye it, and to cause her to trauaile before her time. Tenthlie: if without iust cause they graunt to such as are weake of body to breake the Fasting daies, and to eate flesh in Lent or vpon other daies prohibited. Eleuenthly: if they counsaile their patients to to doe any act whereby they shall commit a deadly sinne: as to haue carnall copulation when they be vnmaried, or to be drunke^, etc. Twelfthly: if they require too exceeding great stipend or fee for their counsaile, and paines. Thirtienthly: if they take a stipend of any priuat person inhabiting in any City, or towne, where they haue an ordinary stipe^d allowed by the same citie, or towne. Fourtienthly: if they giue not freely their counsaile and paines vnto such sicke perso^s as be very poore. Fiftienthly: if they appoint the sick person to buy moe medicines than he needeth, vpon any compact betwene them, and their Apothecaries.
The Apothecaries:Apothecaries. let them accuse themselues, if in compounding of medicines they put not such things therein as the Phisitian prescribeth, but one thing for an other, or corrupt stuffe, whereby either death ensueth to the sick person, or prolonging of his sicknesse, and disease.

The Marchaunts:Marchants let them accuse themselues of their vnlawfull trafficke, of theyr vniust and deceitfull buying and selling, etc.
In like manner let all other persons accuse themselues in their Confessions, each one according to his state of life.


Generall Aduertisements, whereby to know, and discerne, which is a deadly sinne, and which is a ueniall sinne.
IN all these kindes of sinnes that haue bin here noted, it is needfull to declare, which is a deadly sinne,Wee are bound to confesse all deadly sins. and which is a veniall: forsomuch as we are bound of necessity to Confesse all deadly sinnes, but not veniall sinnes, vnlesse we will: But because this cannot be well declared in few words, it shall suffice for this present to giue some generall aduertisement, concerning this point, leauing the rest vnto the iudgment of the wise and discreet Ghostly Father.
Now to vnderstand which is a deadlie sinne, and which is a veniall sinne, there are wont to be giuen these two Rules following.
The first and most generall rule is,The first Rule. that whatsoeuer is co^trary to Charity, is a deadlie
 sinne. By Charity,Whatsoeuer is contrarie to Charitie is a deadlie sinne. wee vnderstand the loue of God, and of our neighbour: wherfore, according to this Rule, whatsoeuer is against the honour of God, or the profit of our neighbour in any matter of importance, is a deadly sinne.
As to do or speak any thing that may discredit his good name, or fame, or to hurt him in his goods or landes, or such like: for this quencheth Charity, wherein consisteth the spirituall life of the soule. And therfore it is rightly and aptly called a deadly sin, because it taketh away the spirituall life: but whatsoeuer is not against Charity, but only besides Charitie, is a veniall sinne:What a veniall sin is. as idle wordes, which hurt no man: or some kind of little vaine glory, of anger, of negligence, or of glottony, I meane, to eate a little more than is necessarie, or such like.
The Second Rule.The second rule is more speciall: which is, that whatsoeuer is contrarie to any one of the Commaundementes of Almightie God, or of the Catholicke Church, is a deadly sinne. As that which is done contrary to the Commandement, that saieth: Thou shalt not steale:Exod. 20. or thou shalt not commit adultery, etc. Or that which is done contrary to the Commandement of the Catholicke Church: which commaundeth vs to
 pay tithes: to confesse our sins to our own Pastor, or to some other, with his licence, at the least once euery yeare, to receaue the most blessed Sacrament at Easter: to Fast in Lent, and vpon other dayes appointed for Fasting.Summa. S. Thomae. 1. 2. Quaest. 88. Art 6 and 22. qu 66 art 6. in responsione ad tertiu^ argumentu^. Et Nauarr: in Manuali Confes. Cap. 11. Numer. 4. and Cap. 17. Numer. 3. But it is diligently to be noted, that that which is of his own nature a deadly sin, may be a veniall sin, by one of these two waies: to wit, either because the matter is but small, and of little importa^ce, (as if one should steale a cluster of grapes, or a pin, or a point, or such a like triffle:) or because the worke is imperfect, by reason that it wanted a full co^sent, and deliberation: as it may happen in euill thoughts, without any consent giuen thereunto, but yet euil resisted: for which cause, that which of it selfe was a deadly sin, is by the imperfection of the work, no more than a veniall sin. Likewise here it ought to be co^sidered, that there be three kinds of co^mandements:Of three kinds of co^mandeme^ts. wherof some are negatiue: as, Thou shalt not kill, etc. which do bind vs euer, and for euer: that is in euerie time, and at al times: others be affirmatiue, as to giue alms: to haue contritio^ for our sins: to loue almighty God,Summa. S. Thomae. 1. 2. quaest. 100. Art. 10. and 2. 2. quaest. 33. Artic-2. and these do bind vs euer, but not in euery time, and at all times, but onely in time of necessity, and then are we
 bound of duty to doe them.Soto, de Iustitia, and Iure. lib. 2. quest. 3 Artic. 10. There be others, which are compounded both of the one and the other: to wit, both of negatiues, and of affirmatiues: as to restore other mens goods. For this commaundeth to restore, and commaundeth also not to withhold our neighbours goods, and these and such like Commandements doe bind vs to obserue them both manner of waies, to wit: euer, and at all times. And therefore it is not sufficient for him that is in debt, and ought to restore, to haue an intent and purposed minde to make restitution in time to come: but it is necessary that he doe restore forth with: because he ought not to retaine the goods, or landes, which doe belong vnto another, against the will of the owner: the which is a Commaundement negatiue, which bindeth vs euer, and for euer, that is, at all times: wherefore, he that retaineth after this sort the goods or lands of others, let him well consider his owne case, and let him make restitution out of hand, and without all delay, as wee haue declared.




HERE FOLLOWETH A briefe maner of confession, to help such persons as vse to be Confessed oftentimes.


Accipite spiritum sanctum, quorum remiseritis peccata remittuntur eis, and quorum retinueritis retenta sunt. Iohn. 20.22. Multi credentium veniebant confitentes, and annunciantes actus suos. Act. 19.18.



THE III. CHAPTER.
HAVING now treated of Confession, for the behalfe of such persons as doe vse to be Confessed very seldome times in the yeare, it followeth that we do also declare, after what manner such as are commonly Confessed euery weeke, or fourt-night, or very often-times in the yeare,
 ought to prepare and examine them-selues. Among which sort of persons, there be many sore vexed and troubled with scruples, because in examining their consciences, they finde not sometimes whereof to make their confession. For knowing and beleeuing certainely on the one side, that they are not without sinnes, and not finding on the other side at the time of Confession any particularities of them: whereof they might be Confessed, they are in a great perplexitie, and scruple of minde, and doe fully perswade themselues, that they were neuer truely and rightly Confessed.
Causes of scruples in confession.Why this so falleth out, we may assigne two causes: the one is, because it is in deed a very hard matter for a man to know him selfe, and to vnderstand throughly all the secret corners of his conscience: For which cause, the Prophet spake not in vaine, whe^ he saied Delicta quis intelligit? ab occultis meis munda me Domine:Psal. 18.13. and 14. Pro. 24.17. That is to say, who is hee that know^th his sinnes? deliuer me O Lord, from my secret offences. An other cause is, because the sinnes of iust persons (of vvhome the wise man saieth, that they fall seuen times in the day,) are rather sinnes of omitting, than of committing. The which kinde of sinnes are very hard to be knowen.

But for the better vnderstanding of this matter, it is to be noted, that all sinnes are committed by one of these two waies: to wit, either by way of Committing: tha^ is, by doing any wicked deed: as by robbing, killing, committing fornication, etc. Or by way of Omitting: (that is, by leauing some good thing vndone: as for not louing god, not fasting, not praying, not hearing of Masse, etc.) Now, of these two kindes of sinnes, the first, (because they consiste in doing) are very sensible, and easie to be knowen: but the second kinde of sinnes, (consisting not in dooing, but in omitting or leauing vndone,) are much harder to be knowen: because that thing vvhich is not, hath no meane to shew it selfe, for to come to light. Wherefore, it is not to be maruelled at, that spirituall and deuout persons (especially if they be simple,) doe not finde some-times in examining theyr consciences any sinnes, whereof they may accuse them-selues in theyr Confession. For these persons not falling so often into those sinnes of committing,) whereof we haue spoken,) and the other sinnes which be of Omitting, being not easie to be vnderstood, hereof it commeth, that they know not wherof to make their confessio^,
 and therefore are they so grieuously vexed.
Wherfore, for remedy hereof I thought good to ordeine this Memoriall, for the instruction of such persons: wherein is chieflly treated of those kinde of sinnes, which are of Omitting. And because these sinnes may be, eyther against God, or against our selues, or els against our neighbours, I haue therefore deuided the Memoriall into three parts, which doe treate of these three kindes of negligences. Among which negligences, there be manie which sometimes are not so much as veniall sinnes: but yet they are imperfections, and defects, and oftentimes they may be veniall sins. And therefore such as walke towardes perfection, should not whollie pretermit in their Confessions, to accuse themselues of them. Howbeit, this is not conuenient to be done at all times, but at certaine times, (and especially vpon principall Feastes,) for otherwise wee should weary our Ghostly Father ouermuch with the superfluous length of our Confessions: but at other ordinary times, whe^ we come to Confession, euery man may take hys choyce out of these negligences, as he shal think may best serue for the dischargeing of his conscience in that behalfe.


Here followeth the Memoriall, to help such as come oftentimes to confession.
Accusations in the beginning of Confession.
AFTER that he hath sayed his generall Confession,How a sinner may begin his confession. and before hee enter into a particular accusation of his sins, let him accuse himselfe of these foure thinges following.
First, for that hee commeth not so vvell  prepared vnto this Sacrament, and for that he hath not vsed such diligence in the examining of his conscience as hee ought to haue done.
Secondly, for that he hath not such sorrow  and repentance for his sinnes, neyther yet such a firme determination and purpose vtterly to forsake sinne, as hee ought to haue.
Thirdly, for that he came not vnto the  most Holy and blessed Sacrament of the Aultar to receaue the same, with such purity of conscience, and with such reuerence, and deuotion, as became him: and for that hee hath not had after the time of receauing such a close recollection of minde, as was requisite for so high a ghest.
Fourthly, for that hee hath not vsed so  great diligence in the amendment of his life, nor endeuoured to profitt himselfe
 daily more, and more in the seruice of God: but hath rather continued in one verie same luke-warmenes, and negligence, yea and waxed worse, and worse also. These accusations being said, let him begin to accuse himselfe in such order as followeth.


Sinnes by way of Omitting towardes God.
TOWARDES Almighty God we are bound to haue these three Theologicall vertues, Faith, Hope, and Charitie. And as concerning each one of these, a man may accuse him-selfe in this manner following.
As touching Charitie,Charitie. let him accuse himselfe, for that he hath not loued Almightie God with all his hart, and with all his soule, as he was bound to doe: but hath rather bestowed his loue inordinately vpon creatures, and vanities of this world, forgetting his Lord, and Creatour.
As touching Faith,Faith. let him accuse himselfe, if hee haue not had such a stedfast, and firme Faith, as hee ought to haue had: and if hee haue not banished out of hys minde with all speed all such fantasies, and thoughtes, as whereby the diuell endeuored to make him stagger in matters of
 Faith, and to swarue from the Catholicke Church.
As touching Hope,Hope. let him accuse himselfe, if in his troubles, and necessities that haue happened vnto him, he haue not had recourse vnto our Lord, with such an assurance, and confidence, as he ought to haue done. And if he haue bin discouraged in his minde, and taken griefe and sorrow for them out of measure: for this proceedeth of the weakenes of his hope, and confidence in God.
As touching Puritie of intention,Puritie of intention. let him accuse himselfe, for that he hath not done the workes apperteyning vnto the seruice of God, with such a pure intention (that is to say, for the loue of God only) as was requisite: but that he did them some-times, as it were for manners sake, and at other times, for custome only: and some-times, because they liked vvell his owne taste, and appetite: or for some other like respectes.
Let him also accuse himselfe,Diuine inspirations. for that he hath bin too slack, and negligent in answering to the inspirations and callings of Almighty God, resisting often-times therein the Holie Ghost, because hee would not enforce himselfe, and take a litle labour
 and trauaile. This is a fault, which is verie spirituall, and secret, and very meete it is, that wee should alwaies haue a conscience thereof.
VnthankefulnesIn like manner let him accuse himselfe, for that hee hath not bin so thankefull for his diuine benefits, as hee ought to haue bin: and for that he hath not rendred due thankes for the same, nor taken such benefit by them, as the rather to loue and serue him the better, vvho is the giuer of all thinges.
Let him likewise accuse himselfe, of his forgetfulnesForgetfulnes. of our Lord, hauing him oftentimes, as it were quite banished out of his heart: whereas we should alwaies haue him in his presence, and set him continually before his eyes.
Impatiency.As concerning patience in aduersitie, let him accuse himselfe, if peraduenture he haue not had ^uch a sufferance in bearing patiently all such aduersities, and troubles as it hath pleased Almighty God to send him, and if hee haue not acknowledged, that they were sent from his hand, for his further commodity: and if he haue not giuen him such thanks, as for the same were due vnto him. This matter may be specified more at large, if his conscience take remorse of any particular thing.

Moreouer, let him accuse himselfe, for that hee hath not behaued himselfe vvith such reuerence and deuotion at Masse time, and other diuine seruice, and in Holy places, especially in the presence of the most blessed Sacrament, as he ought.


Sins by way of omitting towards himselfe.
A MAN consisteth of many partes. For he hath a body, with all his senses, and a soule, with all her appetites, and a spirit with all his powers, which are vnderstanding, memory, and will: And so he may offend against the right gouernment and order, which he ought to haue kept in euery one of these.
First of all, let him accuse himselfe, for that he hath not gouerned his body with such rigour, and seuerity, as hee should haue done, as well in eating, drinking, clothing, and sleeping, as in all other thinges: but hath rather bin very gentle and fauorable towards the same, and a very delicate cherisher of himselfe.
Let him accuse himself, for that he hath not kept both his imagination and senses so closly recollected, and ordred, as they should haue bin: but hath suffered them to range and wander abroad in matters of
 pleasure, and delight: as in hearing, seeing, talking, and imagining of many thinges, which were idle, fantastical, vaine, and nothing to the purpose, the which doe afterwardes hinder the close recollection of the minde, and the attention vnto praier.
Let him accuse himselfe also, for that he hath not mortified his appetites, and resisted his own will, as he ought to haue done: but hath rather followed, and contented the same almost in euery thing.
Let him accuse himselfe, for that hee is not so humble in his minde, and in his workes, as he should be: And for that hee hath not esteemed himselfe for so vile, and miserable, as he is indeed, nor handled himselfe, as such a one hath deserued.
Let him accuse himselfe also, for that he hath bin so flouthfull and negligent in praier, and for that he hath oftentimes giuen ouer, and left off the same, vpon small, and light occasion: and for that he hath not bin at the time of prayer with such a closenes of minde, and diligent attention thereunto, as of duty was requisite.


Sinnes by way of Omitting towards our neighbours.
LET him accuse himselfe: first, for that hee hath not loued his neighbours vvith such
 loue, as hee would looke that others should loue him, according as almightie God hath commaunded.
Likewise, for that hee hath not succoured them in their necessities, with such reliefe, and help, as he should, and might haue done.
Also, for that he hath not taken such pittie, and compassion vpon their miseries, and prayed vnto almighty GOD for them, as he was bound to doe.
Moreouer, let him accuse himselfe, for that hee hath not had, nor felt in his minde such an inward griefe, and sorrow, as hee ought to haue had, for the publike calamities of the Catholicke Church, as Schismes, Heresies, Rebellions, Warres, Sacriledges, etc: which haue beene stirred vp in our vngratious age, by Luther, Zuinglius, Caluin, Beza, and other Heretikes: and for that it hath not grieued him euen at the bottome of his heart, to see so many christian soules daylie deceaued by their diuilish preachings, and bookes.
Furthermore, let him accuse him-selfe, for that he hath not prayed vnto almightie God for the extirpation of all Schismes, and Heresies, and for the conuersion of Heretickes vnto the Catholicke Faith, as he was bound to doe.
Such as haue Masters, and superiours, let them accuse themselues, for that they haue not obeyed the^, and reuerenced the^, as they ought to haue done.
Such as haue children, wardes, schollers, or seruants: let them accuse themselues, for that they haue not instructed and chastised them, and prouided for them all such things as were necessarie, as well for their instruction in the doctrine of the CATHOLICKE Church, and preseruing them from all infection of Schisme, and Heresie, as also for all other vvorldelie necessaries, and for
 for that they haue not bin so circumspect and carefull ouer them, as their duty required: considering that Almighty God wil demaund a straite account of them in this behalfe.


Of Sinnes of committing.
AFter that the penitent hath in this wise accused himselfe of his sinnes of Omitting, then may hee begin to accuse himselfe of those sinnes which are called sinnes of Committing: running ouer the tenne commaundementes, and the seauen deadly sinnes, and accusing himselfe in such of them, as wherein his con^cience shall be most mooued, and prouoked so to doe. And if he will goe more briefely to worke, then may he examine his thoughtes, wordes, and deeds, wherein he shall thinke that he hath offended, and so accu^e himselfe of the same.
After all this, hee must accuse himselfe of all such sinnes, as are commonly apperteyning vnto that state, and office, that he is of* declaring wherein hee hath offended against the lawes and dueties of his state. As for example, if hee be a Religious person, let him accuse himselfe, if hee haue broken his three vowes of Pouertie, Chastitie, and obedience, or any other thing belonging to his Rule. If hee be a Iudge, Sergeant, Counsellour, Atturney, Aduocate, Phisitian, or Merchaunt, etc. let him accuse him-selfe of such thinges as appertaine to his Office. If he be a Prince or Ruler, let him accuse himselfe as concerning his gouernement.
When he hath ended all these accusations, let him then conclude as followeth, saying: As wel for all these sinnes, as also for all others, wherin I haue offended my Lord GOD, in thought, vvorde,
 or deed, I accuse my self to be a most grieuous sinner, and doe acknowledge my selfe to haue offended Amighty God through my default, my great default, yea, my most grieuous default: and therefore I desire you my Ghostly Father, to giue mee absolution and pennance for the same.



OF OVR SATISFACTION. An Explanation of the Doctrine of the Catholike Church, concerning the Satisfaction of penitent sinners, for the Temporall paine remayning sometimes by the iustice of God for the^ to suffer, after that their deadlie sinnes committed after Baptisme, and the euerlasting paine due vnto the same be forgiuen. @. 1.
INTENDING to make an introduction for the better vnderstanding of the Churches doctrine concerning the satisfaction of penitent sinners, I thinke it very conuenient, to giue warning to the christian reader, to take diligent heede of the heretikes common slaunderous and crafty dealing in treating thereof: whereby they haue circumuented great numbers of the vnlearned people, and alienated their mindes from the Catholicke Religio^, to giue credit vnto their new heretical doctrin.
For first in treating in their bookes and sermons of our workes of satisfaction, they make no distinction or difference at all,The deceitfull dealing of heretikes, in treating of Satisfaction. in what state the works of satisfactio^ are done: whether in the state of deadly sin, or in the state of grace, neyther yet doe they distinguish betweene satisfaction for the fault of sin, and satisfaction for the paine of sin: nor whether the workes of satisfaction are to be done for satisfaction of the euerlasting paine, or for
 satisfaction of the temporall paine.Note the Churches doctrine co^cerning our Satisfaction. Whereas the Churches doctrine is, that none of our workes be satisfactory vnto God for any of our deadly sins, vnlesse they be first abolished by the grace of god: because no workes done in the state of deadly sin, (being then done by an enimie of God) can satisfie God. For vnlesse the person be first reconciled and gratefull vnto God, his workes of satisfaction can not be gratefull and acceptable vnto him: but when the workes of satisfaction be done by a penitent sinner in the state of grace, then it is to be presupposed, that the fault of the deadly sin committed by him after Baptisme, and the euerlasting pain due vnto it, be already abolished by the grace of God, by vertue of our Sauiour Christs satisfaction communicated vnto him. And then his good Christian vertuous workes of Fasting, Praier, and almes-deedes; etc. being done by him in the state of grace, (as a member of Christ, and an adoptiue sonne of God,) are vnited vnto Christs satisfaction, and be then very gratefull and acceptable vnto God, and doe satisfie his diuine iustice for the temporall paine remayning for a penitent sinner to suffer, when his sorrow and contrition for hys sinnes is not so feruent, and perfect, as by order of the Diuine IVSTICE is prescribed, and required.
And note well, what I affirme, that these painefull vertuous workes of satisfaction done by a penitent sinner be satisfactory vnto the diuine iustice,Our workes of Satisfaction be onely for the guilt of temporall paine, and not for the guilt of euerlasting paine in Hell. only for the guilt of temporall paine, and not for the guilt of euerlasting paine in Hell, (as the Heretikes doe falsly slaunder the doctrine of the Catholicke Church,) Because the guilt of euerlasting paine euer accompanieth the deadly sin, (as the shadow doth the body,) and is euer pardoned
 vnto penitent sinners at the very same instant whe^ the deadly sinne is pardoned.Vide Concil. Trident. Ses. 6. Cap. 14. and Can. 30. and Ses. 14. Can. 14. and 15. I meane hereby that the euerlasting continuance of the paine is in such wise pardoned in penitent sinners, that it ceaseth to be euerlasting, and is chaunged into a temporall paine onely.
And let no man maruaill, that some times a temporal paine remaineth for a penitent sinner to suffer, after that his deadly sinne,Summa. S. Thome. 3. part. quest. 69. artic. 3. and the euerlasting pain due vnto it, be forgiuen him. For if of original sinne, which is forgiuen by the Sacrament of Baptisme, there doe afterwardes remaine diuers temporall penalties to the person that is sanctified by that Sacrament: the which temporal penalties be sorrow, feare, labour, hunger, thirst, diseases, and euen death it selfe, all which doe trulie vexe and afflict vs, and be after a sort a kinde of temporall paine, that came vnto vs by originall sin:Sap. 1.13. and if of the same original sinne there doe remaine also certaine reliques in them that be Baptised, left by God in them, for their exercise, proofe and merit, as Concupiscence, or fomes peccati, (as the learned diuines tearme it,) which remaineth in our members, striuing against the law of our mind, why should anie christian Maruaill then, that the Church affirmeth, that sometimes a temporall paine remaineth for a sinner to suffer, after that his sinne committed after Baptisme is forgiuen him by his confession in the Sacrament of penaunce.
For otherwise if the sinne be neuer forgiuen before the paine, but that both the sinne and all paine due vnto it be alwaies forgiuen iointly together at one instant, (as the Heretikes affirme,) then would it follow very euidently, that so long as the paine should endure,Note that these Holy men had their sins for giuen them, and yet suffered afterwardes temporall paines for them. so long would the sinne endure also. Wherfore sith Adam, Moyses, Dauid, and
 diuers others suffered for their sinnes committed against God very great temporall paines during al their whole liues, according as by almightie God himselfe was prescribed vnto them, it would then follow hereupon, that their sinnes were neuer forgiuen them vntill the very last end of their liues, and that fro^ the very time they committed their sins vntill they died, they were neuer the true seruants of God, but remained during all their whole liues out of his grace, and fauour. The which false assertion, being so contumelious vnto such Holy men, no christian ought once to imagin, sith the Holy Scriptures affirme, that vpon their repentance for their sinnes they had forgiuenes of them, and were Holy men, and in the fauour of Almighty God, notwithstanding that they suffered afterwards during their whole liues, certaine grieuous temporall paines for their sinnes, according as Almighty God himselfe had prescribed vnto them.
Ezech. 18.20. Deuter 14.16.Againe, it i^ to be noted, that according to the true sence of the Holy Scriptures, all learned Diuines doe agree, that the personall sinne of the Father is not tran^ferred vnto his children, vnlesse they consent vnto the same sinne: But yet they affirme,Exod. 20.5. Ex^d. 347. Numer. 14.33. 1. Reg 2.31. 1. Reg. 3.14. 2. Reg. 12.13. and. 14. Thren. 5.7. that the paine appointed by Almightie God vnto the father for his sinne, is some times transferred vnto his posterity. As appeareth in diuers places of the holy scriptures, and namely where it is affirmed, that God visiteth the iniquity of the Fathers in their children, vnto the third and fourth generation of them, etc. as also in an other place where it is said in the lamentations of the Prophet Ieremie. Cap. 5. verse. 7. Our Fathers haue sinned, and be not, and we haue borne the iniquity of them. And therfore it is a kind of malicious madnes in the heretiks, to affirme so directly, and expresly against the Holie
 Scriptures, that the sinne, and all paine due vnto it, be lincked in such an indissoluble society together, that no guilt of temporall paine remaineth at any time vnto a penitent sinner, after that his sinne is forgiuen him.
Wherefore, as Philippe Melancthon a Luthera^,Melancthon in locis communibus: de Satisfactione See the puritanes second reply against D. whitgifte. pag. 172. in his booke of common places, and likewise the Puritane Caluinists, in a late printed Inglish booke haue hereupon recanted, and written very earnestly against the new opinion of their fellow protestants herein, and doe protest, that God oftentimes remitting the faultes vnto penitent sinners, doth neuertheles punish them some times for their faults all the daies of their liues, and not only in their own persons, but some times in their childrens, and in all that belonged vnto them: so my aduise is vnto all other Heretikes to recant their new fond opinion also, and to humble them ^elues vnto the auncient approued doctrine of Christes Catholike Church, and in no wise to presume, to prescribe to almighty God in what maner he should worke, either in giuing of remission of sinnes, or in doing of Miracles, or in anie other of his workes, but to submitte all vnto his Holy will, and ordinaunce: sith what^oeuer he worketh, is freelie and without any necessity. We knowe, that the world and the ornament thereof, are the worke of God, and yet fewe things in it are brought to their last and full perfection altogether at one instant: as we see in herbs, trees, fishes, beasts, and in all other thinges, that doe daylie increase, and decrease. And thoughe it be graunted,Summa. 5. Thome. 3. part. quest. 86. artic. that God in his Miracles, cureth the whole man perfectlie, both in body, and soule: yet maie we obserue, that as touching the circumsta^ce of time, he worketh diuersly therin, as appeareth in sundry Miracles wrought
 by our Sauiour Christ.Math. 8.14. Luc. 4.38.Christ healed some persons whollie at one insta^t and some other in progresse of time.Marc. 8.24. Marc ^.25. For some persons he healed out of hand, and wholy at one instant: as Saint Peters Mother in law and diuers others: And some again he healed not forthwith at one insta^t, but in progresse of time, a: he did the blind man, of whom Saint Marke writeth, that first his sight was restored vnto him imperfectly, and therefore he saied, I see men walking as it were trees: and afterwardes he was fully restored vnto his perfect sight, insomuch as the Holy Scripture saieth, he sawe al things clearely. And in like maner doth Almightie God deale in diuers sorts with penitent sinners, that haue offended him with committing any deadly sin after their baptisme, graunting vnto some of them a more ample pardo^, than vnto others, according to their earnest sorrowe and contrition for their sins, and their charitie and zeale vnto his Seruice, and honour. Wherein there is very great diuersity among penitent sinners. And therefore thoughe almightie God for Christes sake doe freely pardon all penitent sinners their sinnes, and the euerlasting paine of Hell due vnto them: yet some-times he punisheth some penitent sinners afterwardes with temporall punishment for their sinnes when their Conuersion and contrition be not so feruent, and perfect, as it ought to be. And some-times againe, when hee seeth a great feruent compunction and perfect repentance in a sinner for his offence, hee then not onlie pardoneth him his deadlye sinne, and the euerlasting Paine in Hell, due vnto it, but the guilte of all temporall paine also therewith: As it is probablie thought he did vnto Sainct Marie Magdalen and the Theefe vpon the Crosse, who shewed diuers wonderfull and extraordinarie rare signes of meruilous great inward compunction, and sorrowe
 for their sinnes,Few penite^t sinners be so feruent in their co^uersion, and contrition as Marie Magdale^, and other Saincts haue bene. and of a most feruent loue and xeale vnto the seruice and honour of our Sauiour Christ. And would to God, that both I, and all other sinners, would with the assistaunce of his grace earnestlie endeuour to haue such perfecte Contrition for our sinnes as they had, and then should wee not neede afterwardes anie other Satisfaction for punishment of our sinnes, either in this life, or in Purgatorie. But, sith all penitent sinners be not ordinarilie so feruent in their sorrowe and contrition for their sinnes, as they, and diuers other Saincts haue benne, why should others presume to looke for so ample a pardon at God his hand, for their most grieuous sinnes, being not by many degrees so perfectlie contrite, and penitent for them, and consequentlie not so worthie to haue so ample a pardon.
For the verie cause why penitent sinners are ordinarilie bounde by order of the Diuine iustice to doe Satisfaction vnto God for the guilt of temporall paine,Note the cause why p^nite^t sinner^ are ordinar^ly bound t^ doe Satisfa^tion vnto God. remaining for them to suffer, after that their deadlie sinne, and the euerlasting paine in Hell, due vnto their sinne, be pardoned them, is for that very fewe penitent sinners haue so earnest, so feruent, and so perfecte contrition, and compunction for their sins, when they doe repent and conuerte them selues vnto God, as that their contrition, and abhorring of their sinnes, and their conuersion vnto God, doe proceede from them with all their hartes and with all the forces of their souls, in such degree of perfection, as almighty God prescribeth, and requireth according to our possibilitie, hauing a merciful regard therin to the conditio^ of this life, and of our humaine frailty and to the measure of his graces, which he of his goodnes and mercy giueth vnto vs, to strengthen and assist our weak forces in al our spiritual motions and exercises, apperteining
 to the fulfilling of our duty in his seruice
Wherefore, in respect of their imperfect contrition for their sinnes, the iustice of almighty God requireth afterwards of them a temporall punishment, to be suffered either in this life, or in Purgatorie: whereby to reduce them fullie againe vnto the right order of the diuine iustice, vvhich by theyr sinnes they haue transgressed, and broken. Forsomuch (as S. Thomas very learnedly noteth,Summa. S. Thomae. 12. quaest 87. Artic. 6. and 3. part. quaest. ^6. Artic. 4.) the inordinatenes of a fault is not reduced vnto the due order of iustice, but by reco^pensing it with paine: for it is meet by due order of iustice, that he that hath obeyed and followed his owne will, more than hee ought, doing thereby against the vvill of God, should either willingly, or vnwillingly suffer contrary to that which hee would. And when the contrition of a penitent sinner for his sin is not so perfect, as by the iustice of God is prescribed, in regard whereof a temporall paine is required of him. It is certaine, that vntill such time as the same temporall paine due vnto his sin be payed, the sin is not fully and perfectly remitted: for that a sinne includeth in it (reatum culpae, and reatum paenae)(...) sinne in^ludeth in it ^eatum cul^e, and reatu^ ^aenae. the guilt of offence, and the guilt of paine, and vntill both of them be wholly, and fully remooued away from the sinner, the order of the diuine iustice is not fully repayred in him.
And the way to repaire and reduce againe penitent sinners vnto the order of the diuine iustice, when their contrition for their sins is imperfect, is by suffering afterwardes temporall paines, and afflictions: whereby they may as members of Christ, and by vertue of his aboundant satisfaction, and redemption vpon the Crosse, satisfie after a sort, and in their degree, the iustice of almighty God: for such Temporall paines as hee requireth of them
 to suffer, by reason of their imperfect contrition for their sinnes.
And note well, that I say, that such penitent sinners may doe satisfaction vnto God after a sorte, and in their degree, for their temporal pains: and that I say not,Note that penite^t sinners cann^t doe Satisfaction vnto God in a most absolute iust Equality. that they may doe Satisfaction vnto God in a most absolute perfect iust equality. For albeit I graunt, that a christian cannot with equall payment doe satisfaction vnto God for the inestimable great benefits he hath receaued of him: As for his benefits of creation, conuersation, redemption, uocation, and other his manifold benefites: nor for his deadle sinne: and the euerlasting paine due vnto it: neither yet with equiualent paiment for the temporall paine which he is bound to paie: forsomuch as thc Philosophers affirme, we cannot render either vnto God, or vnto our parentes, of whome we haue receued our being, iust and perfect equality of paiment, (as in case I owe tenne pounds, to render iust tenne pounds, or the iust value thereof againe:) yet neuerthelesse, a christian being in the state of grace, may as a member of Christ, and adoptiue sonne of God, by vertue of the grace of God, and of the merit of Christs Satisfaction, make sufficient satisfaction vnto God, with his vertuous painfull workes, according to certaine equalitie (not of value, or of quantity,) but of Proportion.Note that(...) penitent si^ner may do^tisfaction^to God, w^ assistance his grace,^cording(...) certaine^quality o^ proporti^ correspo^ vnto his ability and forces. I meane hereby: that like as God doth towards vs, that which becommeth his goodnes, and omnipote^cie^ euen so we may render vnto him that which our possibility can beare. And in this wise, looke what Proportion there is from the benefites of God, vnto God that bestoweth them vpon vs, euen so the like Proportion of our paiment is required by God, acording to our possibility: wherfore, lik as for the benefits we haue receaued of God, it is sufficient
 for vs to doe Satisfaction vnto him for the iniuries we haue committed against him, according to our forces, and his grace, assisting and strengthening vs for the same.
God requireth no further Satisfaction for vs, but according to the measure and proportion, of o^r forces and his grace, assisting vs therin Genes. 4.7. Ec. 15.14.15.16.17. and 18. Eccl. 31.10. Psal. 31.9. Psal. 80, 11: Psal. 94.8. Ezech. 18.31. Mat. 12.33. Mat. 23.37. Luke. 7.30. Iohn. 19.10. Act. 7.51. Rom. 12.21. 1. Cor. 7.36.37. 1. Cor. 9.17. Ephes. 4.30. Iac. 4.8. 1. Iohn. 3.3 Ad Philemo ^em. 14. Heb. 10.26. ^poc. 3.20. ^poc. 20 17. ^od accept^th our ver^ons actio^s and workes done with his grace as ours, in that hee hath made vs Lordes of them. Mat. 10.20. Rom. 8.26. 1. Cor. 3.9. 1. Cor. 15* 10. 2. Cor. 3.5. 2. Cor. 9.8. Gal. 2.20. and 21. Phil. 2.13 Phil. 4.13. 1. Ioh. 2.29. 1. Iohn. 3.1. and 24. 1. Iohn. 4.16. Note, that God requireth not all such thinges of vs as hee might require. Mat. 19.12. Mat. 19.2^ Act. 4.34.35. 1. Cor. 5.25. 1. Cor. 9.15.16.And this maner of Satisfaction is of such sufficient qualitie, as the goodnes, wisedome, and Iustice of Almightie God (in regarde of the condition of our humaine frailty) hath ordeined, prescribed, and accepteth for sufficient.
And albeit whatsoeuer we giue in Satisfaction vnto God, wee haue receaued of him: yet forsomuch as he hath created vs according to his owne Image, and likenes, and hath endued vs with reason, and free will, that thereby we should be lords of our owne actions, and things, we may therefore giue our actions and things vnto him as ours, in that he of his great clemencie and bountifulnes hath made vs Lords of them, and accepteth them as ours.
And I graunt, that it were very great arrogancy in vs, in case we shuld affirme, yea, or once Imagin that by our owne naturall forces alone we are able to doe Satisfaction vnto God: for that were to incline to the errour of the Pelagians. But it is no arrogancie nor errour at all to saye that after wee be made the Members of Christ, by his grace, whereby our sinnes and the euerlasting paine due vnto them are forgiuen, wee may then doe Satisfaction vnto God, for the temporall paines prescribed for them. Because therein we arrogate nothing properlie vnto our selues, but doe attribute all vnto Christ, our sweete Sauiour, and Redeemer, who giueth vs grace, both to beginne and accomplish our satisfaction. And then we doe satisfaction vnto God, as Members of Christ, not by our spirit, but by the spirit of Christ.

And withall, in the consideration of our Satisfaction, wee must diligently note the wonderfull goodnes and mercie of Almighty God towards vs: in that he requireth not all such things of vs, as he might lawfully require, but hath onlie prescribed and limited vnto vs a certaine measure of bond, as necessarie to our saluation: to witte: the keping of his commaundements, and a fewe other things, without which his commaundementes can not whollie and dulie be kept. And as for the works of perfection, which by way of counsell only are propounded in the gospell vnto vs, though almighty God might haue required them of vs by way of precept, in case hee would haue delt seuerelie with vs: yet such is his vnspeakable goodnes and clemencie towardes vs, that he would not bind vs of necessity vnto them. Wherefore, sith we maie doe some vertuous painfull workes, ouer and besides those that be commaunded vnto vs by Almighty God: for example, we may freelie giue or not giue either half or all our goods or lands to the poore: and freelie fast, and praie, at such times as we are not bound thereunto by precept* and freely absteine from manie things, which are and maie lawfullie be vsed,) therefore with some painful vertuous workes of abstinence, not otherwise required necessarilie of vs by almightie God, wee may do Satisfaction vnto him, for the guilt of temporall paine remaining for vs to suffer, after that the deadlie sinne and the euerlasting paine in Hell is pardoned vs.


An answere to the place of the eightienth Chapter of Ezechiel, alledged commonlie by the Heretickes against our doing of Satisfaction.
 @. 2.
 BVT against this approued doctrine of the catholicke church, the heretikes doe commonly obiect a place of the holy scripture, taken out of the 18. chapter of Ezechiel, where almightie God saieth: If the wicked shall doe penance for all their iniquities, and shall keepe all my commaundements, and shall doe iudgement and iustice, etc. I will not remember their iniquities.Ezech. 18.21.22. Wherupon they argue, that in case God require of a sinner any te^porall paine for his sin, after that his sin is forgiuen him, then he reme^breth the iniquitie of the wicked after his doing of pennance.
Hereunto we make foure answeres.  First, that this  promise is made by almighty God vpo^ this Condition, to wit: If the sinner shall doe penance for his sin: but perfect pennance comprehendeth in it satisfaction vnto God for the sin, therefore the sinner doth not perfect pennance, that satisfieth not for the guilt of  temporall paine due vnto his sin. Secondly we answere,Ezech 18.21. and 27. that a condition is also limited here to the sinner in these words. Si impius custodierit omnia praecepta mea, and fecerit iudicium, and iustitiam: that is to say: If the sinner keepe all my commaundements, and doe iudgement, and iustice: which doing of iudgement, and iustice, is performed by doing of painfull works  of satisfaction. Thirdly we answere, that albeit we admit, that no mention is made here of any satisfaction for sin, yet it followeth not therefore, that no satisfaction ought to be made vnto God for sin^ forsomuch as the Prophet Ezechiel maketh no expres mention here of Faith, or of Hope, or of Charitie: neither yet of many other vertues, which be all very  necessary for the obteyning of life euerlasting. Fourthly we answere, that in that he saieth, he will not reme^ber the iniquities of the wicked, he meaneth that he wil no more account the penitent sinner
 for his enimie. But this promise hindreth not, but that he may punish a penitent sinner after his reconciliation into his frendshippe, though not in seuere maner, with euerlasting damnation, as hee punisheth his enimie, yet in a Fatherly louing maner, with temporal correction, as a Father chastiseth his child for his fault. According as Saint Paule very plainlie affirmeth, saying.Heb. 12.9. Deus flagellat omnem filium quem recipit: that is to say, God skourgeth euery child, that he receaueth. Meaning hearby, that whereas by the Sacrament of Baptisme wee are become the Children of GOD, in case any of his children doe aftewards sinne deadly against him, though he like a most louing Father doe receaue his penitent childe into his fauour againe, and pardoneth him very gratiously the fault of his deadlie sinne, and the euerlasting paine in Hell due vnto it* yet because ordinarile his penitent children conceaue not so great and perfect sorrowe and compunction for their sins as is required for them, (as S. Peter, Mary Magdalen, and other Holie Saints haue done for their sins) therfore (speaking ordinarily) he scourgeth euery child, that hee receaueth, with some temporall paine for his sin.
And according to this exposition, are all other authorities in the holie Scriptures to be expounded, where it is affirmed, that God casteth our sins behind his back: and into the bottome of the Sea,Isay, 1.18. Isay 38.17. faey 44.22. Mich 7.19. etc. For these and other like places be properly referred to the sacrament of baptisme, wherein both the sin, and all paine due vnto it, are altogether remitted: yet in case they be referred to the Sacrament of pennance, then are they to be expounded, that in the iustification of a penitent sinner, Almighty God doth mercifully forgiue all the sin co^mitted by him after his baptisme, without retaining the least parte
 of it. but as touching the paine due vnto it, though hee will not punish his reconciled childe as his enimie, but doth mercifully forgiue him the euerlasting paine in hell: yet to con^erue his iustice, and to make his children more careful from falling into the like deadly sinne againe, hee chaungeth the euerlasting paine, into a temporall paine, and ^o chasti^eth his childe in a Fatherly louing manner, whom hee receaueth mercifully againe after Baptisme into hi^ grace, and fauour. And in this vvise the saying of the Prophet Dauid is verified. Misericordia and veritas obuiauerunt sibi, iustitia and pax osculatae sunt.Psal. 8.11.


That the Heretickes Obiection, that neyther our Sauiour Ch^ist, nor his Apostles, enioyned any worke of Satisfaction vnto sinners for their sinnes comm^tted before baptisme, is no cause, but that Christs Priestes may enioyne Workes of Sat^sf^ction vnto sinners, for the Temporall paine due to their sinnes committed after their baptisme. @. 3,
 AND whereas some heretikes haue ohiected, that forsomuch as neither our Sauiour Christ, nor his Apostles enioyned any ma^ner of Sati^faction vnto sinners for their sinnes, therfore no painful works of Satisfaction ought to be enioyned vnto any christian that sinneth deadly after Baptisme* I answere,  that this is a deceitfull obiection, deuised by the Heretickes, to beguile the ignorant simple people.
And for the better vnderstanding of their deceit herein, the good christian reader must co^sider and note very dilligently, that when any Iewes, TVRKES,Concil. Trident. Sess. 14 Cap. 2. and 8. and Can. 14 and 15. and Se^^. 6. Cap. 14. or other INFIDELS, doe first come to the christian religion, and be baptised, the Catholicke Church teacheth, that all their sins committed before their Baptisme, and all manner of paine due vnto those sinnes be forgiuen them by the Sacrament
 of Baptisme: but in case they sin deadlie after their baptisme, that then the iustice of God, requireth they should be receaued vnto mercie after another manner, and that though vpon their repentance, their deadly sin, and euerlasting paine due vnto it be mercifully forgiuen them, that yet by order of the diuine iustice, when their sorrow, and contrition for their sinnes is not perfect, they must then suffer some temporall paine for the same deadly sin. And certainely by very order of iustice it is meete,The iustice of God requireth more seuerity to be vsed to such as sin deadly after Baptisme, than to such as sin before Baptisme. that such sins as are committed by Infidels before the knowledge of the truth, before the clouds of darknes are expelled out of their minds, before they be deliuered out of the bondage of the diuell, before they haue receaued the Christian faith and religion, before they haue made any promise to Almighty God, not to sin deadly, and before they be adopted to be the sons of God, and incorporated into Christ, as his members by the sacrament of Baptisme, should haue a more ample, and more free remission, with greater mercy and pardon, than such sins as are so vngratefully committed by christians after they haue receaued of almighty God, all these inestimable diuine benefits afore-said. And our Sauiour Christ himselfe hath signified the same vnto vs in the gospell of S. Luke, saying.Luk. 12.47 That seruant that knew the will of his Lord, and prepared not himselfe, and did not according to his will,Summa. S. Thomae. 3. part: quaest. 86. art. 4. ad tertium argumentum and in addit. quaest. 2. art. 6. and tertium argumentum and quaest. 18. Artic. 2. shall be beaten with many stripes: but he that knew not his will, and did things worthy of stripes, shall be beaten with few. And the reason of this difference is, because in the sacrament of baptisme (in which we are as it were regenerated, and borne a new, as new creatures in Christ) we be incorporated into Christ with a greater coniunctio^ than in the sacrament of penance: and so we receaue of him greater grace in Baptisme, than in Penance.

Mat. 9.9. Luke. 7.47. and 48. Act. 9. Luk. 23.24 Act. 2. Act. 4. Iohn. 8.11.And by this distinction we may easily conceaue the reason of diuers examples specified in the holy scriptures, wherein it appeareth, that greater mercy and pardon hath bin shewed to some sinners, than to others: For whereas wee read in the Holie Scriptures, of Mathew the Publican, of Marie Magdalen the sinfull woman, and of Paule, and of the theefe vpon the Crosse, and of many others to haue bin receaued by our sauiour Christ into hys grace, and fauour, without any satisfaction, and that S. Peter did the like vnto such as were baptised by him, and that our sauiour Christ said nothing els to the adulterous woma^, but go and sin no more, the reason hereof is, because they sinning before Faith, and Baptisme, were after those sins receaued vnto the christian Faith: but shew mee others in the Holie scriptures, that sinned deadly after they had receiued the Christian Faith, and Baptisme, and then shall ye finde it otherwise.
As for example, let vs consider of S. PeterS. Peter. the chiefe of the apostles, doe we not reade in the gospell, that after he had denied Christ, he went forth, and wept bitterly for it?Luk. 23.62 Yea, and though at that time vpon his so bitter weeping and earnest repentance for his sin, he had his sin forgiuen him: yet he wept afterwards so much, and so often for that sin, that as S. Clement his owne scholler writeth of him, hee vsed euer afterwards, vntill his very death, when he heard the Cocke crow to call to minde at that time his denying of Christ, and to rise vp then to weep and to pray. And as S. Peter himselfe was euer thus mindfull of purgeing his own sin past, and still iudged, and punished himselfe afterwards very grieuously for it, with such a continuall austere pennance during his whole life:2. Pet. 1.9. so in his second Epistle he counsaileth very earnestly all christians also
 not to forget the purging of their old sins past.
And we may likewise note, how S. Paule did not receaue againe the incestious Corinthian,The incestious Corinthian. who was a christian, but after his great heauines, and sorrow, and publike reprehension for his sin by many christians: and therefore writing thereof in his second Epistle to the Corinthians hee sayeth. To him that is such a one, this rebuke sufficeth that is giuen by manie.2. Cor. 2.6. Where the Apostle calleth it a rebuke giuen by many to that incestious Corinthian, for that all the christians in Corinth being many did shun from all conuersation and communion with him, which rebuke was very grieuous vnto him, and yet patiently suffered by him.
Now consider here I pray you, doth not the Apostle very plainely signifie in this place,Mat. 3.8. Luke. 3.8. 2. Cor. 7.9. and 10. that the incestious Corinthian had shewed fruites worthy of penance, and suffered punishment enough for his sin, in that with so great long sorrow and heauines of mind for the same, he had bin shunned by many of the Corinthians, and that this being patiently and humbly suffered by him, was a sufficient satisfactio^ for his temporal punishment: and therfore S. Paule required the Priests of Corinth to absolue him,2. Cor. 2.6. Note that penite^t sinners in the Primitiue Church confessed first their sins to a priest, and he afterwardes enioined th^ to doe Pennance for their si^^^s: but he did not absol^e them vntill saying: sufficet ei. This rebuke sufficeth.
And if S. Paul had thought (as the caluinists do) that there is no need for any sinner to suffer at any time, any more paine for his deadly sinne after that it is forgiuen him, why did he not commaund the Priests of Corinth to absolue the penitent Corinthian forthwith: so soone as he heard that hee was sorry and repentant for his sin: especially sith God euer pardoneth the deadly sin forth-with without any delay, vpon a sinners sorrow, and repentance for it: as appeareth in Dauid and in Manasses, and in diuers others? And why did saint Paule delaie
 from absoluing that incestious Corinthian vntill he might say: This rebuke sufficeth that is giuen by many vnto him, to the end that he may be absolued? If the outward rebuking of that incestious Corinthian by many, being added to his inward sorrow, and repentance for his sin, was sufficient for his absolution, then by S. Paule his doctrine somewhat wa^ted before vnto hi^ inward sorrow and repentance for his sin, and that was this outward pennance to be shunned by many christians, from all conuersation and communion with him, vvhich vvas his temporall punishment, and Satisfaction for his sin.


That it appeareth by the p^actise in the Primitiue Church, that the Workes of satisfaction enioined in ancient time by Byshoppes and Priestes vnto penitent sinners, were to this end chieflie, that they should thereby doe Satisfaction vnto Almightie God, for the guilt of the temporall paine remaining for them to suffer for their sinnes committed after Baptisme. @. 4.
SOME of the Heretikes by reading the auncient holie Councels,  and bookes of the auncient holy Fathers, and Ecclesiasticall Histories of Christs Catholicke Church, and finding in them, that in all ages since Christes Ascension into heauen vntill this our corrupt age, penitent sinners haue bin euer taught, and enioyned by the holy Bishops, and Pastors, in all Churches throughout christendome, to doe satisfaction, doe graunt that in the Primitiue Church, and in other ages afterwardes, diuers austere ^atisfactions haue bin enioyned vnto penitent sinners for their publike notorious sins: as appeareth in the auncient Cou^cell of Ancyran, and in the first Councell of Nice, and in diuers other Councels: but they deny that they were enioyned with this intent, to doe any satisfaction thereby vnto God, for the guilt of
 theyr Temporall paine, but onely to satisfie the church, and their neighbours, by doing of publike pennance, whom they had offended, and ^candalized, with their publike notorious sinnes.
I an^were,  that their owne con ciences accuse them, that this is but a deceitfull cauill And I hope in God to make the same very euidently to appeare here to euery discreet christian reader, that is not wilfully blinded and bewitched with theyr new licentious, and carnall Heresies^ for all the ancient holy Fathers of Christs Catholike church, were of this iudgement, (as appeareth not only in their bookes, but also in the auncient Councels,) that such publike satisfactions for publike notorious sins, were done in such wise by the penitents to satisfie the church, and their neighbors, that with al, they were chiefly done to the inte^t that the penitent sinners might doe s ti^factio^ vnto God with the^: as appeareth very plai^ly by the rites, ceremonies, and praiers, with which such publike Satisfactions were done in the primitiue Church For the bishoppe, and cleargie, vsed, when such publike Sati faction^ were performed, to postrate the^ selues vpon the ground and with feruent praiers, and teares, to make humble request (not vnto the people, but) vnto Almightie God, to graunt vnto such publike penitents full pardon of their sinnes. And commonlie they v ed to say the Seauen penitential Psalmes for them.
And for a more euident proofe, that this doing of satisfaction was chiefly intended, and directed to doe thereby satisfaction vnto God, it appeareth not only by the rites and praiers vsed therein, but also by theyr manner of doing Satisfaction. For such publike sinners in the Primitiue church, did not only publike penances for their publike notorious
 sins, but also very many priuate and secret penaunces for them, wherewith they did satisfaction for their temporal punishment in secret wise vnto God only.Concil. Anciranum. Can. 4. And for proofe hereof, when the Auncient Cou^cell of Ancira ordeined, about the yeare of Lord. 308. that such christians as were constrained by the officers of Pagan Princes to offier sacrifice in the temples of Idols,Ibid. Can. 5. and did suppe there among the Infidels, should doe three yeares penaunce. And that such christians as were compelled to goe thither,Ibid. Can. 8 and did not eate there among the Infidels, should doe two yeares penance: and that such christians as yeelding to compulsio^ did the second and third time offer Sacrifice vnto Idolls,Ibid. Can. 9 should doe fower yeares penance: and that such christians as did not only them selues offer sacrifice vnto Idolls, but perswaded other christians also to doe the like,Concil Nicenum. Primum. Can. 11. should doe ten yeares penance: and also when the first Nicen Councell ordeined, that such christians as fell from the christian Religion, and yeelding to become Idolators. either volu^tarily, or for feare of confiscation of their lands, or goods, or for other like daunger should doe seauen yeares penance.Concil. Elibe^inum. Can. 22. and. 46.
