And when the Auncient Eliberin Councell ordeined, that such christians as fell from the Catholike Church into Heresy should doe ten yeares penance, what learned wise man in reading these decrees of these ancient holie cou^cells can otherwise conceiue, but that the penitents did manie secret penances during the yeares prescribed vnto them to doe penance for these publike sins, besids their publike Penances? But the Caluinists wil say, that they doe not conceaue so, but that the intent of the auncient councells was onlie, that the publike penitents should doe publike penaunces, during al^o those yeares, to satisfie only the Church,
 and their neighbours: and that the penitents did not any priuat secret penances for their publike sinnes during all the yeares of penaunce prescribed vnto them. And this cauiling shift they haue deuised, because in case they should grant, that publike penite^ts did any secret penances also for their publike sins, then were it euident, that those secret penaunces were enioyned them to doe satisfaction onlie vnto God, and not vnto the Church, or their neighbours, who could not be satisfied by any certaine knowledge whether those secret penances were performed, or not.
But before I proceede in the confutation of this new cauilling shifte of the Heretikes, I must needes tel them hereby the way, that they be deceiued in their argument, when they argue, that forsomuch as publike penitent sinners did with their publik penaunces satisfie their neighbours, therefore they did no satisfaction with them to God. I say,Publike penite^t sinners by their publike penaunces did Satisfaction both to God, and the Church. It is a greater difficulty to a sinner to doe Satisfaction publikly tha^ secretly. that this argument wil deceiue none, but the simple ignorant people, being nothing worth in the indiffere^t iudgement of any wise man. Because the publike maner of doing satisfactio^, doth not any thing weaken but much more strengthen, and increase the force of true satisfaction vnto God: in that the, satisfaction which is done, not onlie vnto Godp but ioyntlie there with also in publike wise to our neighbours, is of greater force, and efficacie, than the sati^faction that is done in secret wise vnto God onlie: by reason of the greater difficultie, shame, paine, and griefe, that commonlie synners haue in doing satisfaction publikelie, than in doing it onlie secretlie. And withall it is to be noted, that not onlie the discipline of the Church but the iustice of God requireth also, that such wicked dissolute
 per^ons as are neither ashamed, nor afraide, to sin publikly, to the publik scandal and offence of their neighbours, should do publike penance for it, that thereby they may doe satisfaction both vnto God, and their neighbours together.
And now for an euident confutation of the Caluinistes new cauilling shift, and to proue, that publike penitents in their manner of doing penaunce in the primitiue Church, did not only publike penaunces for their publike sinnes, but very manie secret penaunces also for them, I desire the Caluinistes to read an Auncient decree,S. Leo. pp. 1. ad Rusticum NarBonense^ Episcopum. Epist. 90. Cap. 17. made about the yeare of our Lord. 461. by Saint Leo the Great, the first Pope of that name, wherin it is ordeined that such christians as were onlie present at the Feaste-of the Gentils, and eated of the m^ates offered vnto Idols should be enioined fastings for that grieuous sinne.Concil. Epaunense, tempore Gela^i. sp. 1. Can. 29. Let them read also Concilium Epa^nense? holden in the time of Pope Gelasius, the first pope of that name, wherein it was decreed, that such as fell into heresie, should not be admitted againe vnto the aultar, vntill they had done two yeares pena^ce fasting euery third day. Let them read also Conciliu^ Toletanum. 8. wherein it was decreed, that who so without necessity eated flesh in Lent, should be debarred from receiuing the most blessed Sacrament at Easter, and from eating of flesh that time of the yeare.Concil* Toletanum. 8. Ca^. 9.Concil. Turonense, tempore Caroli Magni. Can. 22. Concil. Cabilonense tempore Ca^oli Magni Let them read likewi e Concilium Turonense, wherein certaine priests be reprehended, for not enioining fastings and abstinence vnto penitente sinners, according to the quality of their sins. Let the^ read also C^ncilium Cabilonense. 2. in the 35. canon, wherein it appeareth, that the vse of flesh, and wine was forbidden vnto penitents. And in the 45 canon of that councell, and in the 2. canon of the Auncient Councel of Laodice, it appeareth al^o, that the vse was to enioine penitent sinners in co^fession
 to say praiers, to giue almes. Moreouer,Can. 22. concil. Cabilonense, tempo e Caroli Magni. can. 35. 45..Concil Laodicoen. cad-2 Concil. Triburiense. Can. 55. 56. 57. and 58. let them read Concilium Triburi^ns^, wherein it ordeined, that if any committed wilful murder, hee should doe very austere penance for seauen years and that for the first 40. daies he should be debarred from entering into the church, and eate nothing els during tho^e 40. daies, but onely bread and salt: and drink nothing els but pure water: and weare no linne^, but onlie in his breeches, or stops: and that after those 40. daies, he should not be admitted to enter into the church during one whole yeare: and that he should absteine during all that time from flesh, cheese, wine and from ale, or bere, except vpo^ sundaies, and holy dayes: and other like penances be enioined to be done in the rest of the Seauen years. And withal let the Heretickes read the 25. and 26. canons of the Councel of wormes,Con. worm. Can. 25. 26. Concil. Magunt. can. 16. and the 16 canon of the Councel of Maguns, holden in the time of the Emperour Ranu^phus, wherein diuers particular penaunces be prescribed for such penitent sinners, as killed either their father, or brother, or any priest. Among other, these priuate and secret penaunces are there enioined the^: to wit, that they should not eat any flesh during their liues: and that they should fast euery day, sauing Sundaies and holie daies, vntil three a clock afternoone, and absteine from wine, and ale, or beere, etc. many other auncient councelles might also be aledged, to proue, that not only publike penances, but also many secret penances were enioined vnto publike sinners to be performed in secret wise, to the end they should do satisfaction thereby vnto God for the gilt of their te^poral paine remaining for them to suffer for ther sins: but these holy auncient cou^cels may suffice to perswad any good christian herein, be hee either learned or vnlearned. Now let the caluinists tel me, for what end
 these auncient councels prescribed vnto publike sinners,Publike sinners were enioyned to do not only publike pena^ces, but also very many priuate and secret pennances. besides their publike Pennances, to doe so many priuate, and secret pennances also for their publike sinnes, in case it were onely to satisfie their neighbours? If the auncient councels had none other intent nor end by their enioyning of publike pennance vnto publike sinners, but onely that they should thereby satisfie their neighbours, vvhat neede had they to enioyne vnto publike sinners, Prayers, Fastings, wearing of Haire-cloth, and other secret austere penances, which were done by the penitentes in secret wi^e from all knowledge of their neighbours?
To satisfie their neighbours only, the penitents needed no more, but some publike externall doing of Pennance, or to haue acknowledged publikely their fault vnto their neighbours, and to desire openly pardon of the^, or of the whole Church, whome they had scandalized vvith their publike deadly sin: and they needed not to be enioyned by the priests do for the same such secret austere pe^nances, of Praiers, Fastings, wearing of haire-cloth, and such like: which were not done publikely, and apparantly to the ope^ sight of ther neighbours, and therefore their neighbours not knowing certainlie whether they were performed or not, could not be satisfied by him.
But to preuent all cauils of the Heretickes, if it may be, what cauils can they possiblie deuise, to shift off the pennances which were enioyned by the priestes in auncient time vnto penitent sinners in confession for their secret sinnes:Secret pennances were enioyned for secret sins to doe thereby Satisfaction vnto God, and not to their neighbours. as for secret murders, secret adulteries, secret theftes, secret periuries, secret slaunders, etc. which deadly sins being done in secret, were vtterly vnknowen to their neighbours, and so they could not be scandalized
 by them, and consequently they needed no satisfaction for them.
Here they must needes graunt, that the pennances enioyned in ancient time by the Priestes vnto penitent sinners in confessio^ for these secret deadly sinnes, were to doe satisfaction vnto God only, and not vnto their neighbours, who were vtterlie ignorant of these secret sinnes.Concil. Cabilonense. 2. Can. 32. As for example, Concilium Cabilonense. 2. holden in the time of Carolus Magnus, ordeined, that penitent sinners should confesse vnto Priestes, not only such sinnes as they committed by external acts of their bodies, but euen such sinnes also as they offended only in their thoughts: as their wicked malicious thoughts of treasons, adulteries, fornications, thefts, reuenge desiring other folkes deaths, or to haue their houses, offices, landes, or goodes, the which being fullie purposed and consented vnto, are grieuous deadly sins before almighty God, albeit they were neuer actually performed. Now the Priests iudging by hearing the varietie of sinnes, (as S. Ierome saieth,S. Ieronim. Super Mat. cap. 16. Concil. laodicen. Can. 2. Co^cil. wormac. Ca^. 7. Concil. Cabilonense. 1. Can. 8. Co^cil^ consta^tinop. 6. Generale. Can. 102.) did (as the holy Councels ordeine) enioyne pennances vnto penitent sinnnrs, according to the heinous qualitie of their sins. And sith the Priestes enioyned praiers, fastings, almesdeedes, wearing of haircloth, and other secret austere penaunces, for publike sinnes, no wise man can then deny, but that they enioyned like secret penauncs also for secret sins of the same kinde, and qualitie, whether they were secretly committed in act, or only purposed and consented vnto in thought. And these secret penaunces were done by penitent sinners to doe satisfaction thereby only vnto God, for their temporall punishment, and not to satisfie their neighbours, who were vtterly ignorant of those secret sins, and so needed no satisfaction for them. And
 told our Lord onlie such sinnes as were confessed vnto him. It appeareth hereby, that Saint Ambrose heard secret confessions of sinnes, made by penitent sinners vnto him alone: and that he kept the sinnes ^ecretly to God, and him selfe only, that were confessed vnto him: and consequentlie, that he would enioyne them to doe secret penaunces for their sinnes: the which being graunted, then it followeth, that they were enioyned to do thereby satisfaction vnto God.Concil Toletanum 1. Ca^. 6. And likewise, when Concilium Toletanum primum o^deined that Religious women should haue no familiarity with their Confessor: as it appeareth thereby that they confessed their sins vnto him. so is it euident also, that the confessions were made in secret, of sins done by religious women in their Monasterie, which is in secret, as of the sins of pride, disobedience, enuie, anger, and of other secret sins, and consequently that their penaunces were both enioyned and performed in secret, to do satisfaction thereby only vnto God.
And here vtterly to stoppe and close vp the heretikes mouthes, and all their wylie deuised cauills herein, let them read an auncient Councell, called Concilium valentinum,Concil Vale^tinum sub D^maso papa Primo. Ca^. 2. holden in Fraunce, vnder Pope Damasus, the first of that name, wherein it was ordeyned, that Religious women that marry after their vow, must doe first Satisfaction vnto God, by doing reasonable pennance for that sinne, before they be admitted to communnicate. Behold here, that by this Auncient approued COVNCELL, Satisfaction is prescribed in expresse wordes to be done vnto God.Co^cil Romanum. 4. sub S^mmacho Papa. And the same is also affirmed in an other auncient Councell holden in Rome.
If I should here al o alledge all the particular sentences out of the bookes of the auncient Holie Fathers that serue for proofe of this point, I should
 neuer make an end. For the learned know right well, that al the auncient Holie Fathers beleeued, and so taught the christian people in their times, in an all churches throughout christe^dome, that penitent sinners ought to do Satisfaction to God, for the guilt of temporall paine, remaining for them to suffer for their sinnes.
Wherefore Iohn Caluin, the father, director, and principall founder of all the Caluinistes new deuised Hereticall Religion, endeuoureth to perswade all that be addicted vnto his new Sect, that the Auncient Holie Fathers of Christs Church haue in all ages erred herein. These be his own verye wordes here following. Pa^um me mouent,Caluini. Institu lib. 3. Cap. 4. Sect. 38. 39. quae in veterum scriptis de satisfactione passim occurrunt. Video quidem eorum nonnullos, dicam simpliciter, omnes fere, quorum libri extant, aut in hac parte lapsos esse, aut nimis aspere and dure locutos. That is to say. As for all those things that are commonlie founde in the bookes of old writers concerning Satisfaction, they little moue me. I see indeed, that manie of them, I will speake plainly, in a manner all, whose bookes remaine, haue either erred in this point, or spoken too crabbedly, or hardlie. Thus farre be Caluins owne wordes. Whereby the godlie discreete reader maie euidentlie see the p^^ud arrogant spirit of this Heretike Caluin. and how contemptuously he decardeth the long app^oued authority, and graue iudgment, of all the auncient Holie ^athers, that haue Gouerned in Christs Church, not onlie since the first sixe hundred yeares after Christes ascention, (as M^ I^w^ll verie politikelie did delude the ignorant people thereby in his Challenge made at Pau^s crosse in London:) but euen all the aunci^nt Holy Bishoppes, Pastors, and doc^ors that haue ben in all ages, during this fifteene hundreth yeares,
 since Christs time, vntill this our corrupt age. And so Caluin would perswade vs, that all the auncient holy Bishops, and Pastours of Christs Church haue in all ages erred in the doctrine of satisfaction, vntill Frier Luther, and he, and Beza, and other proud fleshly Apostatas, and heretikes, brake their vowes and rebelled against the Gouernours of Christes Catholicke Church, and deuised a new licentious fleshly religio^ in this our vngratious wicked time.
I meruaile, that any wise man, that hath any feare of the terrible iudgements of almightie God, and is carefull of his own saluation, will be so foolishly and blindly bewitched by the diuell, or by his minister Caluin, or any other of his ministers, as to preferre the priuate presumptuous opinion of any heretike, before the graue approoued iudgement of all the ancient holy Bishops, Pastours, and Doctors, that haue gouerned in Christes Church these 1500. yeares, and to imagine that almightie God is now towards the end of the world become either a Lutheran, Zuinglian, Caluinist, Puritane, or Anabaptist,Mat. 28.20* Iohn. 14.16 Iohn. 16.13 1. Tim. 3.15 and that he hath broke^ his solemne faithfull promise made vnto his church, and chaunged his euerlasting holy ordinance, and intendeth now to turne heauen into hell, by thrusting out of hys glorious kingdome of heauen, all the auncient holy Bishops, and Pastours, that haue gouerned and taught the christian people in Christes church, by ordinary lawfull vocation and succession, in all ages since Christs time, vntill this our corrupt age, to intrude therein such arrogant apostata heretiks: as Frier Luther, Zuinglius, Caluin, Beza, and theyr fleshly ministers, which being infamous for theyr dissolute wicked liues, are newly and extraordinarily started vp in our time, as false Prophets, and forerunners of Antechrist, and are directed with a
 contrarie spirit, in deuising a new licentious hereticall religion, directly contrary to the holy approued christian religion of all the auncient holie Bishops, Pastours, and Gouernours of Christes Catholicke Church.


That the vertuous painefull workes of Satisfaction, done by penitent sinners, for the guilt of temporall paine, remayning sometimes for them ^o suffer for their sinnes, co^mitted after baptisme, doe nothing derogate from our sauiour Christs Satisfaction, and Redemption, but doe rather very much commend and extoll the same: forsomuch as they deriue and take from thence their value, force, and dignitie. @. 5.
BVT the most common obiection  of the Heretikes, against our doing of paineful vertuous workes of sati^faction is, that forsomuch as our Sauiour Christ hath sati^fied for vs all, and not onely for our sinnes, but for the sins of all the world, as appeareth* 1 Timothie 2.1. Tim. 2. and 1. Iohn. 2.1. Iohn. 2. therefore (say they) the sinner doth iniurie vnto Christes satisfaction vpon the Crosse, in case he go about to satisfie almighty God for his sinnes.
I answere,  that there be two kindes of satisfaction:Two kindes of Satisfaction. one that deserueth remission of sins, and remoueth away also the euerlasting paine in hell, due vnto sinners for their sinnes. And this sati^fac^ion apperteineth to our Sauiour Christ only, as to our only true Messias, who gaue himselfe for vs,Acts. 4.12. Rom. 3.24.25. Rom. 8.32. 1. Cor. 15.3 1. Tim. 2.5. 1. Iohn. 2.1. 1. Pet. 2.24 that he might redeeme vs with his most precious blood from all our iniquities. And this is the onlie full and perfect satisfaction, for all the sins of all mankinde.
There is another satisfaction, called Sacramentall satisfaction: which is onely to satisfie for the guilt of Temporall paine, required by Almightie God of a sinner, after that his sin, and the euerlasting paine due vnto it, are forgiuen him. This Sacramental
 Satisfaction apperteineth ordinarily vnto al penitent sinners, that committe any deadly sin after Baptisme, when their contrition and detesting of their sins for the loue of God is not so feruent, and perfect, as is prescribed and required by the diuine iustice for the same,
The doctrine of Christes Catholike Church, of the sufficiencie of our Sauiour Christs Satisfaction for all sinnes and for all paines due vnto them. Thoughe Christs passion be sufficient in it selfe for the Redemption of all mankind. yet all are not Redeemed by it with effect. Psa. 80.11 Psal. 94.8. Math. 23.37. Act. 7.15. Ephe. 4.30. Heb. 4.7. 1. Iohn. 3.3. Apoc. 3.20. Psal. 61.15. Ro. 10.21. Isay. 65.2. Isay. 49.4.Now whereas the Heretikes doe obiect, that our christian satisfactory workes be iniurious vnto our Sauiour Christes most precious blood, shedde vpon the Crosse for our satisfaction and redemption, it is an impudent slaunder. For al christians know right wel, that the doctrine of Christes Catholike Church is, that our Sauiour Christe shed his most precious blood, not only to redeme all our sinnes but to satisfie also for all paines due vnto them: and that one droppe of this most precious blood was sufficient to redeeme all mankind: and that the merites of our Sauiour Christs passio^, and the price of his Redemption, and satisfaction, be as it were an infinit treasure, purchased prepared and conserued, for the profitte and vtilitye, of all that are borne into this world. Howbeit we must vnderstand likewise, that though it be sufficient in it selfe for the Redemption of all Mankind: yet is not all Mankinde Redeemed with his precious blood efficaciter, that is to say, with effect As we see by the wicked Iewes, Turkes, Sarazens, Heretikes, Schismatikes, and wicked christians: which are all damned, because they harden their harts in their Infidelity, and wickednes, and doe resiste the good inspirations, and callings, which Almightie God sendeth vnto them, and so doe wilfully refuse the frute and benefit of our Sauiour Christs most sufficient and aboundant redemptio^, and satisfaction.
And of this great iniury, and ingratitude our Sauiour Christ complaineth saying, Pretium meum cogitauerunt repellere. That is to say: They haue purposed
 to refuse my price: and in an other place he saieth: I haue spred forth my hand all the day vnto a people not beleeuing, and gainesaying me. And likewise in Esay he saieth: in vaine haue I labored. Without cause, and in vaine haue I consumed my strengthe.
For in very deed, though this most sufficient and infinit treasure of our sauiour Christs passion, and Redemption, be purchased and prepared for the benefit of all mankind: yet good Reader, wee must all remember, that it beginneth not to be eyther mine, or thine, or any others to be saued thereby, vnlesse Christ be made ours, and we beginne to be truly indeed his seruants, his Members, and sonnes howshold. Because the Merites of our Sauiour Christ be not actually communicated but vnto such only, as be made one body with him: I meane,Christes merits are actually communicated to none other but only vnto his members, that be incorporated into him: and no longer, than they continue vnited vnto him by faith and obedience Heb. 5.9. Ezech. 18.26 1. Tim. 4.1. 1. Tim. 6.2^ vnto such persons, as be incorporated into him, as Members vnto their Head. And his Merites are no longer communicated vnto them. Then they continue vnited, and ioyned vnto him, by Faith, and Obedyence. And so Saint Paule sayeth, that Christ was made vnto all that obey him, cause of eternall Saluation. And in case any christians doe by theyr disobedience fall from Christ, and turne vnto the workes of darknes, and of the flesh. Then are they no more partakers of the Merites of our sauiour Christes Passion, and Redemption, vntill by penaunce they be reconciled and ioyned vnto him againe.
VVherefore (good christian Brother) wee must nor flatter our selues, (as the Heretickes, and dissolute Christians doe,) by considering thys truthe onelie, that our SAVIOVR CHRIST hath by shedding his precious blood in his most bitter passion, and death prepared, and offered vnto his father, a most sufficient
 and aboundant Redemption, and satisfactio^ for all the sinnes, and paines, of all mankind, and that his father doth so esteeme, and accept it: but it behoueth vs also to consider,A medicine helpeth not al sicke persons, but such only vnto Whom it is applied. and imprint this truth likewise deeply in our minds, to wit, that like as a generall medicine profiteth not all persons that be sicke, but ^uch only vnto whome it is applied so our Sauiour Christes most suff^cient Redemption, and sati^faction, prof^teth not all persons in the world, but such only, vnto whome it is effectually applied by such holy meanes, as almighty God hath ordeined, and appointed for the same,
Note, that the vertue of the merits of Christs passion, and death, be not communicated to any christian infinitly nor to all Christians in like Degree.And we must likewise consider, that albeit the vertue of the merits of our Sauiour Christs passion and death, be in itselfe infinit, yet is it not communicated to any christia^ inf^nitly, nor to al christians in equall and like degree: otherwise euery christian should be as iust and holy as the most Blessed virgin Mary the mother of God, or of any of the Saintes: yea euery christian should the^ be infinitly iust, and perfect which is absurd, and false. But the vertue of Christs merits is communicated to some christians in more aboundance, and to some in lesse aboundance, according as euery christian is more or lesse prepared and disposed for receauing of the same, by such holy meanes, as almighty God hath ordeined and prescribed.
And by the ordinance of almighty God, the vertue of the merits of our Sauiour Christs Redemption,by what meanes the vertue of Christs Redemption and Satisfactio^ is to be applied vnto vs. and satisfaction, is to be applied vnto vs for remission of Originall sinne, by the Sacrament of baptisme: and for remission of Actuall sinne by the sacrament of pennance: and for obteining of full remission of temporall paines remaining some-times for penitent sinners to suffer, for want of perfitte contrition for their sinnes, it is to be applied by vertuous
 our painful workes of satisfaction: as by Fasting, Praier, almesdeeds, wearing of hairecloth, whypping our rebellious flesh, and other like good vertuous painfull workes, that be of their own nature painfull and irksome to our flesh.
Whereby it appeareth, that all sinnes,Note, that al sins and all paines that be pardoned to sinners are all pardoned by vertue of the merits of Christs Redemption and satisfaction, applied by diuers meanes, vnto them. and also al gilt of euerlasting and temporall paines, that be pardoned vnto sinners, are all pardoned by vertue of the merits of our Sauiour Christs Redemption, and satisfaction, applied by diuers meanes and waies vnto them. And that the merit of Christs suffering and satisfying for vs, is as it were the life and soule of our suffering, and satisfaction, for the guilt of temporal paines. And that al our painful vertuous workes, had benne, as a bodie without a soule, in case our Sauiour Christ had not by his most bitter passion, and death, satisfied for vs. So as our painful vertuous works of sati^factio^, be neither co^trary, nor iniurious, vnto the satisfaction of our Sauiour Christ, (as the Heretikes doe falslie affirme,) but they be vnited vnto Christs sati^faction, and doe take their vertue, value, force and dignity from the same.
And like as notwithstanding the full and perfecte Redemption and Sati^faction of our Sauiour Christ, our faith, and baptisme,Note, that notwithsta^ding Christs Redemption, and satisfaction, diuers things are also required, as necessary to our saluation, as faith baptisme: keping the commaundeme^ts etc. be required also, as necessarie to our saluation, and likewise the due keeping of God his commaundementes, after we be baptized, and iustified: and withal an inward harty repentance in al such as fal into any deadly sinne after their baptisme, etc. and none of all these doe any whitte deminish the miritte of our sauiour Christs sufficient Redemption, and satisfaction, or be in any respect derogatorie or iniurious to the honour or dignity of his most precious bloud shed for our sinnes: euen so also our externall
 doing of pennance for our sinnes, (which is a signe and effect of our inward pennance,) and our painefull vertuous satisfactory workes (which be purified, and fortified in the most precious blood of our sweet Redeemer, and Sauiour,) doe bring no manner of detriment, iniurie, or dishonour vnto our Sauiour Christs merit, and satisfaction. Forsomuch as by the holy iust ordinaunce of almighty God, our painefull vertuous satisfactory workes be required for our te^poral punishment, in regard of the imperfection of our conuersion and contrition.
Note here the reasons, Why paineful vertuous workes of Satisfaction, be necessarily required of Christians, notwithstanding Christs sufficient Satisfaction.And surely, for very good reason, and for the eschewing of great inconueniences, our painefull vertuous workes of satisfaction be necessarily required of vs, by almighty God, notwithstanding our Sauiour Christs sufficient satisfaction: because otherwise most christians would be very carelesse and negligent in doing of good workes, and would conceaue a security and most certaine assurance of theyr saluation, through the sufficiency of our Sauiour Christs satisfaction, and so they would vse, (as very many doe in their corrupt time of Heresie) our sauiour Christs redemption, and satisfaction, as a cloke, to couer their carelesse slouthfull and dissolute wicked liues, and account all good vertuous painefull workes of prayer, fasting, almesdeedes, and all other painefull doing of pennance, and austere vsage and mortification of theyr flesh, to be superfluous, and in vaine.
But the most principall and singular reason, why some satisfaction is required of penitent sinners by vertuous painefull workes, (as by fruites worthie of pennance) is because our sauiour Christes will is, that the merite of his Passion shall be communicated, and applied vnto christians, so far forth,
 as the order of the diuine iustice requireth. And therefore, forsomuch as our sauiour Christ, hath suffered innocently for our offences, his holy will and ordinance is, (according as reason and the due order of iustice requireth,) that wee that haue bin the offenders, and the cause of his most grieuous and bitter Passion, should resemble, and be like in suffering vnto him, who is our head, our maister, our patterne, and exampler. And this resemblance in suffering with him we ought to haue, as a signe of our gratefulnes, loue, and conformity vnto him, which he requireth of vs, as of faithfull obedient members, mortified with Christ our tormented head, and as a testimony of our hatred of all sinne, and of our zeale and reuerence to the iustice of almighty God.
And our Sauiour Christ himselfe hath reuealed vnto vs in his holy scriptures, that if we will be his members, and conforme our selues vnto him, as vnto our head, we must then imitate him in our liues, and beare our Crosse euery day, and suffer vvith him. And therfore he said: Who so will come after me, let him deny himselfe, and take his Crosse euerie day,Luc. 9.23. and follow me. And note well, that he sayed not, let him take vp my Crosse, but his own Crosse.Note that euery member of christ must ioyne his owne Crosse vnto Christes Crosse, by suffering also with Christ. 1. Iohn. 2.6 That is to say: who ^o will haue any benefitt of the merite of Christs satisfaction, let him apply the same merite vnto himselfe, by suffering also with Christ, and let him ioyne his Crosse with Christs Crosse, and vnite his suffering with Christs suffering: because otherwise wee shall not be partakers of his merites, in case we refuse to be partakers of his suffrings. And so saint Iohn sayeth: He that sayeth he abideth in him, ought him-selfe to walke euen as hee walked. And saint Peter explaineth this following of Christ more plainelie, saying: Christo igitur passo in
 in carne,1. Pet. 4.1. and vos eadem cogitatione armamini. That is to say, Christ therefore hauing suffered in the flesh, be ye also arm^d with the same cogitation. And in another chapter he sayeth: For vnto this are ye called, because Christ hath suffered for vs,1. Pet. 2.21 leauing you an example, that ye may follow his steps. Now how must wee follow our Sauiour Christes steppes? certainely, there is none other way (as I haue ^aid) to followe him, but according as he hath reuealed in his holie scriptures: That is, we must imitate him, not as he is God,Note how we must follow our Sauiour Christs steppes. but as he is man: I meane hereby, wee must imitate his holy life, and beare (not his Crosse, but) euen our own Crosse euery day with him, and drink of the bitter cup of his passion, in suffring with him, as conformable faithfull members to our head. And in this wise we shall be made conformable to the image of the sonne of God. Wherefore saint Paule saieth,Rom. 8.29. Whome God hath forknowne, them hath hee also predestinated to be made conformable to the image of his sonne. And in the same chapter shewing the necessitie of our suffering with Christ, to the end we may be also glorified with Christ, he saieth these words. If sonn^s, heires also: heires truely of God, and coheires of Christ,Rom. 8.17. in case yet wee suffer with him, that wee may also be glorified with him. And in his Epistle to Timothie he sayeth:2. Tim. 2.11. and 21. If we be dead with Christ, wee shall liue also together: If wee shall sustaine, wee shall also raigne together. And if it were not needefull for vs to suffer with our Sauiour Christ, as faithfull members with our head, saint Paule would neuer haue said to the Colossians: I reioyce in suffering for you, and doe accompl^sh those thinges, that want of the Passions of Cbrist,Colos. 1.24. in my flesh, for his body, which is the church. Meaning thereby, that albeit our Sauiour Christ (as our head) hath suffered sufficiently, and though there be no want in our Sauiour Christs Passions,
 which he suffered in himselfe, as our head, for our redemption and satisfaction* yet there ramaineth, and wanteth, that the faithfull members of our sauiour Christ doe suffer also with Christ, their tormented head, to the intent they may be like, and conformable vnto him: for otherwise nothing would seeme more deformed (as S. Bernard affirmeth,S. Bernard. Ser. 5. de omnibus sanctis.) than that delicate members should be ioyned and vnited vnto a head pricked, and tormented with thornes, and other most grieuous and painefull Passions. And in this respect S. Paule said to the Corinthians,2. Cor. 4.10 that wee must alwaies beare about in our bodie the mortification of Iesus, that the life also of Iesus may be manifested in our mortall flesh. And S. Paule himselfe endeuoured so earnestly to beare his Crosse euery day with Christ, and to conforme his life vnto the life of Christ, as a true faithfuil member of Christ, that hee protesteth to the Galathians,Gal. 6.17. that he bare the markes of our Lord Iesus in his body. And so ought euery christian endeuour to beare the markes of christ in his body, (by conforming his life vnto the life of Christ,) and to be vnited vnto him.
And when wee be ioyned and vnited vnto our sauiour Christ, as his true faithful members,1. Cor. 6.17 Qui adhaere^ D^mino vnus spiritus est.Gal. 2.20. so long as we perseuer in that vnion with him, all our good thoughts, actions, and workes, are inspired, directed, gouerned, fortified, and sanctified with his holy spirit. And then like as S. Paule said of himselfe, as of a faithfull member of Christ: Viuo autem, iam non ego, viuit vero in me Christus: that is to say, I liue, now not I: but Christ liueth in me: so may all penitent sinners, being faithful members of our sauiour christ, say in like maner of their doing of vertuous painfull satisfactory works for the guilt of their temporall paines: I satisfie, now not I: but Christ satisfieth
 in me.Note that the Satisfactions of the Members of Christ, be Christes Satisfactions. Because the passions and satisfactions of the true faithful Members of Christ, be Christ passions and satisfactions.
For it appeareth in the Holie scriptures, that there is such a strait Vnion and coniunction betwene our sauiour Christ and his Members, that he calleth the sinnes of his Members his sinnes. As in psalme 21.Psal. 21.1. Longe a salute meae verba delictorum meorum. It is also said in Saint Paule to the Ephesians Cap. 21.Ephes. 2.6. Considere nos fecit in caelestibus, in Christo Iesu: That is to say. He hath made vs sitte with him in the celestials in Christ Iesus. For in that Christ our head sitteth there, his faithfull Members are said to fitte there also: And in the actes of the Apostles our sauiour Christ calleth the persecutions of his Members his own persecutions. And therefore he said to Saule that persecuted the christians after his ascention into Heauen, Saule, Saule cur me persequeris?Act. 9.4. Saul, Saul, why persecutest thou me? Here Saul persecuted not our Sauiour Christ himselfe, but the faithfull Christians his members, and yet our Sauiour Christ accounteth him selfe to be persecuted in the^, he being the lambe (that as S. Iohn sayeth) hath bene slaine in his Members from the beginning of the world.Apoc. 13.8. Mat. 25.40. And so our sauiour affirmeth in saint Mathew, that whatsoeuer is donne to one of his faithfull elected Members, whom he calleth his least brethren is done vnto him.
Note the straite vnion and coniunction betweene Christ, and his true faithfull Members. Eph. 1.23.And after the same manner our satisfactions be Christs satisfactions: for that all the true members, of Christs catholike church are so straitly vnited with our sauiour Christ theyr head, that they together with him are considered as one Mysticall person, and therefore in respect of Christs members, the Church is the plenitude of his person: and
 the passions and sanctifications of Christs members, being dedicated, and sanctified in Christs blood, and sacrifice, make the plenitude of Christs passions, and satisfaction. And so the passions of our Sauiour Christ the head, and the afflictions of his Misticall body the Church, and Members thereof, make one complet Masle of passions, with such great difference for al that betwene the one sort, and the other 'as the high preheminence of our sauiour Christ the Head,2. Cor. 1.5. aboue his Misticall bodye the Church requireth, and giueth. And saint Paul affirmeth, that the passions of Christ did abound in the Corinthians, where he calleth their Passions, the passions of Christ. And Saint Peter exhorteth the christians to reioyce in their communicating (by their sufferings) with the passions of Christ,1. Pet. 4.13. and he calleth these passions, which our Sauiour Christ suffereth in his Members Passiones and Posteriores glorias in Christo: That is to say:2. Peter. 11. the passions and latter glories in Christ.
And in consideration of this straite coniunction and vnion of our sauiour Christ with his Members,Note how one Member of Christ may doe Satisfactorie workes for another. and of the members together among themselues, though one of them can not Merite for an other properly, yet one of them may doe penall satisfactory vertuous works for an other: I meane for the temporall paine required to be suffered by euery member of Christ for his sinne, whe^ their conuersion and contrition be imperfect. Because (according to the article of our creede) there is a-Communion among all the Sainctes. And in respect thereof the prophett Dauid saied to our Lorde:Psal. 118.63. Ro. 15.27. 1. Cor. 12 20. Particeps ego sum omnium timentiu^ te: That is to say. I am partaker of all that feare thee. And the reason hereof is, for that as Saint paull sayeth: though all faithful christia^s are many me^bers of Christ, yet are
 they all but one Misticall body of Christ,Rom. 12.4. and so he calleth them, vnum corpus, and vnus spiritus: that is, one body, and one spirit. And to the Galathians he affirmeth,Ephes. 4.4. that all faithful christians be one in Christ Iesus, and shewing to the Corinthians the cause of this vnion of all faithfull christians in Christ, hee saieth:Gal. 3.27. 1. Cor. 12.13. For in one spirit were we all baptized into one, whether Iewes, or Gentiles, or bond men, or free, and in one spirit we were made all to drinke.
And this communion and participation that is amongst all faithfull christians, as fellow members in Christ, which in our creed is called the communion of saints, is the very ground and foundation, why one of them may (as S. Paule saieth) beare an others burden,Gal. 6.2. and supply the defects of another, so far forth, as apperteineth to the duty of one me^ber of Christ to doe charitably for an other.2 Cor. 8.14 And so saint Paule protested to the Colossians, (vvho were his fellow members in Christ) that he supplied for them in his fl sh^,Colos. 1.24. that which wanted of the Passions of Christ.There is no want in Christs Passions, which he suffered in himselfe, as our Head: but there is wa^t in those Passions of christ, which he dayly suffreth in hys body the Church, and the members thereof. Math. 10.38. Luke. 9.23. Howbeit, God forbid, that any christian should once imagine, that ^aint Paule meant, that there is any manner of want in our sauiour Christs Passions, which he as our head, suffered in himselfe for our satisfaction, and redemption. For Christes Passions were (as I haue said) in that regarde most sufficient, and aboundant. But saint Paule meaneth, that he supplied in his flesh, for his felow members in Christ of the Colossians, in regard of the want of those Passions of Christ, which by his owne ordinance he daily suffreth, and shall suffer to the end of the world, in his misticall body the Church, and members thereof: which by our sauiour Christes owne ordinance, and commaundement, ought to be fellowes of his Passions as they looke to be fellowes of hys glorie: and therefore they ought daily to carry their owne Crosse after Christ, as his
 faithfull Disciples, and drinke of his bitter cuppe,Rom 8.17. 1. Cor 9.27. 2. Ti. 2.11.12 Mat. 20.22 1 Cor. 11.3^. Rom, 2.6. and 8.2. Cor. 5.10. Ephes. 6.8. 1, Pet. 1.^6. Ap^c. 14.13. Apoc. 22.12. and (as saint Paule saieth) ought to iudge themselues before hand in this life, by adiudging to the^ selues some temporall punishment for their sins* as by fasting, watching, praiers, almes-deedes, wearing of hairecloth, whipping their rebellious flesh, etc. and so to preuent, that they may not be iudged for them by almighty God, whose inf^nite goodnesse, mercy, and iustice, be ballanced, and correspondent, in such due order of iust measure one to another, that in no wise hee vvill suffer anie good worke to be vnrewarded, nor any s n vnpunis^ed.
And for a full answere now to the Heretiks,Note diligently this con^^tation of the Hereti^es common deceitfull Argument ag^^nst our doing o^ Satisfaction. Acts. 7.60. Iohn. 17.20.21. Rom. 8.34. Heb. 7.25. 1. Iohn. 2.1. Saint Chri. Ho. 15. ad Rom. Mat 5.24. Luke. 6.28. Luke. 18.1. 1. Thes. 5.25. Colos. 4.3. Ephes. 6.18 1. Tim. 2.1. that doe most wickedly argue against our doing of vertuous painefull workes of satisfaction, affirming them all to be done in vaine, because our sauiour Christ hath satisfied sufficiently for vs: I say, that so they may in like manner argue, that the praiers of all the Holy Martyrs for their persecutors vvere in vaine, and that saint Stephen prayed also in vaine for them that stoned him to death: because our sauiour Christ hath praied sufficiently for al the Elect, and by his praying hath deserued for them all life euerlasting.
And if this cauelling Hereticall argument be admitted, then may the Heretikes argue in like maner, that sith our sauiour Christ, sitting now in heauen at the right hand of his Father, prayeth now sufficiently for vs all, that wee need not therefore to pray now eyther for our selues, or for our persecutors, or one for another, to the end we may be saued, according as our sauiour Christ, and S. Paul, and S. Iames, require of al christians. And what need we then any Churches, or to pray there, or in anie other place, if by our only Faith in Christ, wee be assuredly pertakers of Christs most sufficient praier,, merits, and satisfaction, and neede not to pray,
 merite,2. Tim. 1.3 I^^. 5.16. Act. 15.11 1. Cor. 6.17 1. Cor. 12.3 2. Cor. 3.5. Phil. 2.12. and 13. Apo. 22.11 Iohn. 1.16. Mat. 3.8. Rom. 6.19. Rom. 8.10.26. 1. cor. 9.27. 1. co. 11.13 1. co. 15.10 2. co. 4.10. 2. cor. 12.9. Epr. 2.10 Gal. 2.20. Gal. 5.24. and 25. Phil. 2.12.13. Phil. 4.13. col. 1.24. and 29. Col. 3.3. 1. The. 4.8. 2. Tit. 2.21 1. Pet. 2.21 1. Pet. 1.10 1. Iohn. 3.3. Apo. 22.11 Heb. 12.8. or satisfie in any respect for our selues? Yea if Christes sufficiencie doe take away all meanes on our behalfe of application of the merits of hys Passion, and death vnto vs, then what neede haue we of Faith it selfe, or of preaching of the Gospell, or of praier, or of any other vertuous meanes what soeuer: sith one of them is no more derogatorie to the sufficiencie of the merits of Christes Prayers, satisfaction, and redemption, than the others be?
But the good christian reader shall doe well to blesse himselfe euery day from such deceitfull hereticall arguments. And for the confutation hereof, he must vnderstand, that the praiers of our fauiour Iesus Christ are the fountaines, and foundations, and as it were the vniuersall cause, whereby our praiers are meritorious before the diuine Maiestie, vvhich vvithout the merites of our sauiour Christ vvere of no force, nor efficacie. And all catholickes doe plainely confesse, that all the vertue, dignitie, value, and strength of all our praiers, satisfactions, and good workes, doe proceede from the merits of our sauiour Christ: for as saint Iohn sayeth, De plenitudine eius omnes accepimus: that is to say, of his fulnes we all haue reeeaued. Howbeit, we must note withall, (as I haue before declared,) that the sufficiencie of our sauiour Christes praiers, merits, and satisfactions, are by him ordeined for ^uch, only of the members of his misticall body, as will with his grace endeuour to pray, metite, and satisfie with him, according as is required of them, and to make this more plaine by another example, we all know, that our Christ teacheth sufficiently all truth, and keepeth sufficiently all iust persons: but it followeth not thereof, that there ought not to be any Doctors, Pastours, or preachers in Christs Catholicke Church, to teach vs the
 truth, or that we ought not to be carefull for the due custodie of our hart: for that were to make all christians very careles, slouthfull and dissolute in their liues, and not to endeuour to carrie theyr Crosse, and to worke their saluation with feare, and trembling, but to vse Christs Passion as a cloake and excuse of their wilfull negligence, and wickednes. Whereas our Sauiour Christs will and ordinance is, that all christians should with the assistance of his grace concurre with their Godly endeuours to liue as it becommeth his obedient louing children vnder his holy discipline, and seruice. And so S. Paule affirmeth in these wordes. If you be without discipline, whereof all be made partakers, then are you bastards and not children.
And to the intent wee should continuallie exercise our selues, and perseuere in good christian exercises vnder our Sauiour Christs Holy Discipline and Seruice, he hath prepared and ordeined, (as I noted here before,) that the value of his merits and satisfaction should be transferred, not vnto all his faithfull members a like, but diuerslie, in diuers degrees: I meane to some more, and to some lesse thereof, according to the measure of grace, that he bestoweth vpon them: and according as each one of them endeuoureth with hys grace vnder his holy discipline, to be more or lesse conformable vnto him, in imitating his holy life, And hereof it commeth, that like as all the Elect be not iust and vertuous alike,) for all of them be not so vertuous and iust, as our blessed Lady the mother of God,) so shall they be diuersly rewarded by him in his glorious kingdome of heauen, each one according to the measure of his charitie: For as our Sauiour himselfe saieth: In domo patris mei mansiones multae sunt. That is to say,Iohn, 14.2. In the house of my father, there be many ma^sions of felicity, and glory.

Wherefore, of the premisses we may well conclude, that sith the value and merite of our prayers, and satisfactions, done with the grace of God, doe proceed from the merit, value, and d gnitie, of the prayers, and satisfactions of our sweet Sauour Iesus Christ: and sith his holy wil and ordinance is, that the merit of his sufficient and most aboundant redemption, and satisfaction, should be applied, to haue efficacie in vs, by his sacraments: and by our good workes, donne by his g^ace, which is giuen vnto vs by the Merit of Christ it followeth hereupon, that our vertuous painfull workes of Satisfaction be so far off from diminishing, or obscuring the benefit of our Sauiour Christs Satisfaction, and Redemption, that they doe rather very much commende, and extoll the same. For in that that Christs Satisfaction is the foundation, direction, and worker of the merite, vaine, and dignity of all our good christian works, we by our suffering and satisfying for the guilt of temporall paine, prescribed by his owne mercifull and iust ordinance for vs to suffer vnder his holy discipline for our sins, doe thereby execute Iudgement and Iustice, vpon our selues, according as in Ezechiel wee be required: I meane, by iudging our selues, as S. Paule counsaileth vs, and by punishing, and taking reuenge of our heinous sins vpon our selues, that wee may not be iudged and punished for them by Almighty God. And moreouer we testifie by our vertuous painefull workes of Satisfaction,Mat. 10.38. Mat. 16.24. Luk. 9.23. Mat. 20.22. Act. 14.21. Rom. 6.6. Rom. 8.13.17.29. Gal. 2.20. Gal. 5.24. Gal. 6.14.17. Col. 1.24. 1. Pet. 2.21. 1. Pet. 4.1.13 1. Iohn 2.6. Rom. 8.17.29. 2. Cor. 1.7. 2 Tim. 2.11. that wee (according as his faithfull disciples ought to doe) are willing to imbrace the Crosse of Christ, aed to drinke of hys bitter Cup, and to deny our selues, and to mortifie our rebellious flesh, and to carry our Crosse daily and follow him, after his holy example, as he hath commaunded vs, and so doe endeuour with his grace to liue vnder hys holy discipline, and to imitate the painefull steps of his holy life, and to resemble and be made like vnto him in conforming our selues vnto him, by suffe^ing wi^h him, as true faithful members with our head, to the end we may be also glorified with him, knowing most assu^edly by the holy Scriptures, that in case we be partakers of the pa^nefull Passions of our Sauiour Christ, and doe communicate with him therein, wee shall then be partakers of his consolation also.




Of the third part of the Sacrament of Pennance: which is Satisfaction.

CHAPTER. I.
AFTER Contrition, and Confession,Here the Authour himself beginneth to treat of Satisfaction. How Satisfaction is to be made by vs. followeth Satisfaction, (which is the third part of Pennance:) whereunto appertaineth, to make Satisfaction to the honour of Almightie God, for the offences committed against his diuine Maiestie, by taking iust reuenge vpon him, by vvhome the offence was committed. The reason hereof we declared in the other part, speaking of Fasting, the which we will repeate likewise here, because this is also his proper place.
For the vnderstanding whereof, you must consider, that like as a man, that tra^sgresseth the lawes of a common weale, is bou^d to suffer the penalties appointed for the transgressors of the same: euen so likewise, whosoeuer transgresseth the lawes of Almighty God, is bound to suffer certaine kindes of paines, which are by the iustice of GOD prescribed and appointed for the transgression of them. These kindes of paynes must needes be payed, eyther in this life, or in the life to come: That is to
 say either in Hell,In hell with euerlasting paines. or in Purgatorie, or else in this world. In hell they are paid with euerlasting paines, and torments enduring world without end. In Purgatorie they are not p^ied with euerlasting paines,In purgatory with t^mporal paines but with certaine paines that haue an end, and are limited wi^hin a certaine time. Howbeit these paines in Purgatorie, are so terrible, and so vehement, that (as, Saint AugustineSaint Austine. saieth) there is no paine in this world, that may be compared with them: no not all the cruel paines and torments of the Martyrs, which were the greatest in all the world.
Now from these so great and terrible paines in Purgatorie,How wee may be deliuered fro^ the terrible paines of Purgatorie. we are deliuered by iudging and correcting our selues in this life, with Fasting, watching, praier, discipline, and other austere vsage of our body, although these pains be without comparison farre lesse, than those that are suffered in Purgatorie. For whereas in these things, Almightie God hath regard, not so much vnto the greatnes of the paines, as vnto the will of the Sacrifice:A small voluntarie paine in this life, satisfiieth more than many greater paines suffered of necessity in Purg^torie. (for that such paines as a penitent is content to suffer for satisfactio^ in this world, be volu^tary, but in the world to come they are of mere necessitie,) herof it commeth, why a smal pa ne suffered voluntarily in this life, is without comparison
 of more force, and Satisfieth more in the sight of Almightie God, than manie greater paines, that are suffered of necessitie in Purgatorie, in the life to come.  But yee will say, why Sir? If the sacrament of penance be not sufficient in this behalfe, how is it, that the Sacrament of Baptisme is of such force, as it taketh all away, and absolueth a man quite, both from sin, and from all paine? vnto this questio^ I answere? that there is a great difference betweene the one Sacrament, and the other.  For the Sacrame^t of Baptisme is a sprituall birth, and regeneration of the inward man. The difference betweene the operation of the sacrament of Baptisme, and of the sacrament of Pennance.And therfore, like as one thing that is borne a new, leaueth foorthwith the former being which it had, and receiueth an other new being, and nothing remaineth of that, which it had before: (as when of an acorne springeth a tree, the accorne leaueth his former being) euen so when a man is spiritually borne againe in baptisme, hee leaueth forthwith to be that oldma^, which he was before: for he was before Baptisme the son of anger, wrath, and perdition) and after he hath receaued Baptisme, beginneth to be another new man, to wit the sonne of grace, and so by his new spirituall birth, he is free both from sinne,The sacrament of Penance worketh as a medicine. and from all paine. But the SACRAMENT of Pennance doth not deliuer vs from our
 sinnes past, as a regeneration, or new birth, but as a medicine, which some times healeth perfectly, and some times not, but leaueth behinde some remnantes of the former disease, which afterward with continuance of time, and good gouernment, may be worne out, and consumed away. After this sort doth the Sacrament of Pennance sometimes heale perfectly, and deliuer a sinner both from sinne, and paine, when there concurreth with all a verie perfect Contrition, (such as that Contritio^ of Mary Magdalene was,God pardoneth all the sinne by the sacrament of Penna^ce: but not all the paine, by reason of the vnperfect contrition of the sinner.Note this similitude. and of others the like:) but at other times, (when the Contrition is not so perfect,) though it doe then cancell al the sinne, yet doth it not take awaie all the paine: and so that paine which remaineth vncancelled, for want of perfect Contrition, must be purged either in this life, or in the life to come.
Of this we may take an example euen in worldly affaires: For if a Gentleman do commit an offence against his Prince, for the which he deserueth to suffer the paines of death: yet may he afterwardes doe him such, and so great seruices, as he may deserue his Princes grace, and fauour, and receiue a generall pardon, and cleare discharge from all this punishment. Againe his seruices
 may be such, as he shal not deserue so large a pardon, but some what lesse: which may be, to obteine the Princes grace and fauour, and to exchange the punishment of death into some banishment for a time. After this sort we read that King Dauid pardoned his Sonne Absolon.2. Reg. 14. verse. 21. and 24. For when he had slaine his brother Amnon, and had thereby incurred the iust indignation and displeasure of his Father, after three yeares absence, and banishment hee pardoned him for the offence, which he had committed: howbeit with this condition, that he should not enter within his Princely Palace, nor appeare before his royall presence. Now in like manner, when the Contrition and sorrow of the penitent sinner is not altogether so absolute, and perfect, as it ought to be. Almighty God, by vertue of the Sacrament of Pennance, pardoneth the sinne or faulte committed, and withall, the euerlasting paines of Hell, vvhich through his deadlie sinne he had deserued, (yea, and forgiueth moreouer some part of the temporall punishment:) howbeit, hee will not that such a one shall enter forthwith within his heauenly Palace, and haue there the fruition and glorious sight of his Diuine presence, before such time as he be fullie,
 and perfectly purged, either in this life, or in the life to come, in Purgatorie.
In this wise dealt Almighty God himselfe with the same King Dauid:2. Reg. 12. 13. and 14. God pardoned King Dauid his sinne, and yet punished him afterwardes with temporall paine for it, as with the death of his sonne. Num. 20.12. and 24. Moyses and Aaron, had their sin of mistrustfulnes forgiuen them, and yet for their temporall punishment afterwards for the same sinne, they were for euer debarred from entring into the land of promise. whom (in respect of his Confession, and repentance,) he pardoned the sinne of Adulterie, which hee had committed, and restored him againe vnto his friendship, and grace, which through his sinne he had lost: but yet after all this he sent him great afflictions, and calamities, eue^ for a punishment of the self same sin, which he had before pardoned.
But what sin was there euer in the world more freely pardoned, tha^ the sin of Moyses, and Aaron, at the waters of contradiction? the which notwithstanding, though the sinne were first pardoned, yet the punishment, which the diuine iustice had appointed, remained alwaies fresh in execution against them: which was the debarring of those two holy men, from euer entring within the land of promise. Euen so it happneth for the most part in the sacrament of Pennance, wherein through the vertue of Christs Passion, (which worketh in the same,) the sin is pardoned, and forgiuen, and the grace and fauour of Almighty God is obteined againe: but yet the penitent sinner remaineth stil bou^d, through
 the imperfection of his Conrrition and sorrow for his sinnes, vnto certaine degrees of paine, according as the Iustice of Almighty God hath ordeined.
And though there be many kindes of vertuous workes,And although Moyses praied earnestly vn^o our Lord for it, yet could he n^t obteine his request. As appeareth in Deutron^my. 3.23. and 26. which doe help towards the discharging of this paine, yet doe those especially serue for this purpose, which are most painefull, and most irkesome to our flesh. For (as Saint Gregorie saieth,) because the flesh with his appetites and delightes, hath caused vs to sinne, it is reason that the flesh, being well punished and afflicted for it, should disburden vs from the same sin. And sith that to content our flesh, wee haue discontented and offended Almighty God, reason would, that we should discontent and punish our flesh, to pacifie and please Almighty God againe.


Of the Originall cause of our Satisfaction. THE II. CHAPTER.
NOVV that wee doe vnderstand the necessitie wee haue of SATISFACTION, let vs see the ORIGINALL, and beginning of the same: that wee may thereby the better vnderstand,
 after what sort it ough to be done: For the better perfourmance whereof, wee must call to minde, what we haue spoken before in the beginning of this treatise: to witte, that the true repentance and grace of the conuersion of a sinner, is the greatest grace and mercy, that might be graunted in this life.The conuersion of a sinner is the greatest grace, that may bee graunted to a man in this life. For although glorie be a thing farre greater than grace, (forsomuch as the one is only grace begun, and the other is grace consummated:) yet is it a greater grace for Almighty God to plucke, and deliuer a man from sinne, and to set him in the state of grace, than afterwards when he is receiued into grace, to graunt him glory.
Moreouer, like as Baptisme (which is the first gate, and entrance of the Sacraments, and the beginning of mans regeneration,) bringeth with it (so much as vnto it appertaineth) all the vertues and gifts of the Holy Ghost, ioyntly with grace, fro^ whom all these benefits doe proceede: euen so true Pennance, which is the beginning of our Resurrection, bringeth likewise with it all these gifts, and treasures, and especially a new light and knowledge of things spirituall,Note what ^onderfull ^ffectes doe ^me by ^ue Pen^nce. and diuine: (vnto which thinges before that time man was as it were blind, as liuing in the kingdome of darkenesse, and
 shadow of death.) It bringeth also with it, a new Charitie and loue of God, which is the forme of true Pennance, and of al vertues: and it worketh in our soules wonderfull affections, and feelings apperteining vnto this vertue. For as naturall loue is the beginning of all other naturall affections, and passions: euen so the supernatural loue of God is the beginning of all Spirituall affections and feelinges. And the greater that this supernaturall loue of God is in vs, the greater are the spirituall affections, and feelinges, which it worketh in vs. And as the graces of the Conuersions of sinners be diuers, in some greater, (as the conuersion of S. Paule, S. Augustine, and many others,) in others lesser, (as the ordinarie and dayly Conuersions of sinners, are for the most part wont to be: so are the inward affections, and motions, which this vertue of charity causeth, greater or lesser.
Now this vertue (to witte,Note what wonderfull great effects the loue of God, workeeth in a soule. the loue of God,) causeth in the soule so great a repentance, and discontentation, for that he hath offended Almighty God, that a man would rather, that he had suffered a thousand kindes of torments, than to haue displeased such a Lord. It causeth also a verie great feare of the diuine Maiestie, forsomuch
 much as hee seeth that he hath dishonoured, and prouoked him vnto anger, through such and so many offences, that he knoweth, that he hath thereby incurred the indignation of his furie. Moreouer, it causeth him to be very much ashamed to appeare before his diuine presence, euen as a wife, that hath defiled her Husbands bed, and had bin pardoned for her offence, would be ashamed, when she should be receaued againe into his house.Luk. 18.13 Note, that the loue of God causeth a great vehement desire in a soule to doe satisfactio^ vnto our God with due Pennance, and to be reuenged vpon his owne flesh, that was the cause of his offending of God. For such was the shame, which the Publican in the Gospell had, who durst not lift vp his eyes towards Heauen, for very shame, and confusion of himselfe. It causeth in like manner a verie great vehement desire to make Satisfaction vnto ALMIGHTIE God, with due Pennance, for the offence that hee hath done vnto him, and withall, a very great feruent desire to be reuenged vpon him, that was the cause of this offence: (which was his owne proper flesh. For when hee considereth, how his flesh was the thing, which did with her appetites and inordinate delights entice him to stretch foorth his armes vnto the inordinate loue of creatures, and to diuorce himselfe from the loue and obedience of his lawful spouse, and Lord: then is hee kindled in such sort with an extreame
 fury and rage against his flesh, that he could finde in his hart to rent and teare it in peeces, and with a thousand torments to punish it, for that it hath bin the cause of all his woe.Note this similitude. And that thou mayest the better vnderstand al this matter, imagine with thy selfe, what a chaste noble virgin would doe, if, after that shee had bin espoused to some Nobleman, that were of the blood royall, whom she had neuer seene, but only the Espousalles had bin contracted by Ambassadours in the absence of the parties: and the^ some naughty woma^ should beguile her, and make her beleeue, that shee was betrothed to some other man, calling him by the noblemans name, hee being in deed but a base and rascall fellow, and not spouse: and she beleeuing all this to be true, her should yeeld her selfe vnto him, and take him as her Soueraigne Prince, and louing husband. Tel me now, this noble woma^, that shuld thus be beguiled, in case she should afterwardes perceaue, that it vvas that naughty packe, which had so beguiled her, and brought her to so great a dishonor: what (thinke you) would this noble woman doe vnto that vile drabbe? with what words would shee reuile her? what a stomack would she take against her? vndoubtedly
 she would account it but a small reuenge to drink her blood, that had in this-wise dishonored her. Euen so the soule of the co^uerted sinner, whose eies Almighty God hath opened, and giuen a particular and new light, to see so perfectly and clearly, that Almightie God was her true and lawful spouse, and the last end, for which she was created, and to perceiue on the co^trarie part, that by the deceit of this naughty woma^ (which is her own flesh) she hath bene allured to exte^d the armes of her loue towards creatures, and to embrace them with the self same loue, which was due vnto Almightie God alone, and that her own flesh which was the cause of all this adulterie: how can she haue patience to beare with her flesh? how can she refraine, but with all seueritie to punish and afflict her flesh, yea, and to be fullie reuenged vpon it, that was the cause of her so great miseries: Hereof come those cruel and excessiue chastisme^ts, which some penitents are wont to vse in the beginning of their conuersion from their sinful life: whome yee cannot withhold from their sharpe discipline, from grieuous whipping and punishing their te^der bodies, but they will besides the wearing of heir-cloth, vse great fasting, and abstinence,
 watch, and pray along time together, and frequent manie other kinds of spiritual exercises, in such sort, as they are in danger oftentimes to do great outrages vnto them selues, yea, and to cast themselues downe by such excesse into some fiknes, vnles they take good heed, and be wel warie to keep a measure, and to vse therin verie great discretion.
Such was the spirit of pennance, which Holie Iobe declared in these wordes: peccaui, Quid faciam tibi O custos hominum?Iobe. 7. vers. 20. That is to say: I haue sinned: what shall I do vnto thee, O thou keeper of men? As if he should haue said more plainely, according to the exposition of Saint Augustine.Saint Augustine. O Lord I Confesse my sin. And such is the griefe which I take thereof, that I will not refuse to suffer anie kind of punishment for the same. Consider thou, O Lord, whatsoeuer thy will shalbe that I should do, for I am readie to do all such things, as thy will is that I shuld do. I haue nothing to offer vnto thee, but a hart verie prompt and willing to doe whatsoeuer thou shalt commau^d me. If thou commaund me to cast my selfe into the glowing flames of fire, or this my bodie to be rent and torne in peeces, or to suffer any other kind of torme^t (be it neuer so great)
 I haue an hart redy prepared to fulfill thy will. Here I offer my selfe bound both ha^d, and foot, and I lie prostrate at thy feet: I flee not away: I appeale not from thy sentence: neither do I plead anie thing vnto the iurisdictio^ of thy court. I excuse not my selfe. I make no supplication, that thou shouldest discharge me of my punishme^t: but rather that thou maist iudge me acccording vnto thine owne blessed will Be thou the knife, and I will be the flesh. Hacke me, and hewe me, on which side thou wilt, so that thou pardo^ me the grieuous sinnes, which I haue committed against thee.
In like sort did Holie King Dauid also afflict himselfe, when in one of these psalmesPsalme. 37. vers. 9. o^f penance he saied: I am afflicted, and verie much humbled I sighed from the bottome of my hart. O Lord, before thee is al my desire, and my mourning lieth not hid from thee. My hart is troubled within me, my strength hath forsaken me, and now my sight faileth me. In this wise did this holie penitent afflict himselfe: and so should those likewise afflict, humble, and chastice them selues, that haue offended such a most louing Lord. For (as a Holie Father saieth) the soule, that hath against the wil of God forsaken his Creator, and delighted her selfe inordinatlie in creatures, it is meete,
 that she should purge and repaie with voluntarie paines and trauailes, the voluntarie delights, with which she so blnded herselfe.Paine is naturallie due vnto sinne. And forsomuch as paine is naturallie due vnto sinne, (where with the faulte is corrected, and reduced in order) reason would, that he shoud willingly accept, yea, and endeuour to suffer paines, that was so bold, as to commit so many offe^ces against Almightie God. And sith that m^n hath through sinne forsaken the cheffest goodnes (to wit, Almightie God,) and hath exchau^ged him for a vile creature, (which in verie deed is a great iniurie and contempt of the supreme Maiesty of almighty God) it is reason, that he, who hath despised such a mightie Lord, should humblie, despise, and willinglie abase him selfe euen vnto the dust of the earth.
After this sort then do those take paines to make Satisfaction to Almightie God, whose eies he hath opened with his heauenlie lighte: by meanes of which light, they come to vnderstande, the infinite greatnes and excellencie of the goodnes of Almightie God: and in the same they perceiue the greatnes of their owne malice, and iniquitie: and according thereunto they haue a desire
 to make Satisfaction vnto him. For confirmation wherof, as also for our example, and for a confusion of the carelesnes, and tepiditie of our corupt time, I haue thought good to rehearse here a part of an Historie of the rigorous and wonderfull austeritie of certaine holy Penitents, which S. Iohn ClimacusSaint Iohn Climacus. saw in a Monastery. The which Historie this holie Father reporteth, as being a witnes of sight, in a manner in these vvordes following.
A notable Historie written by the auncient holy father, Saint Iohn Climacus.When I (saith he) came first into this Monasterie, I beheld therin certaine things, which neither the eies of the sluggard haue euer seene, neither the eares of the negligent hard, nor yet may it be co^ceiued within the hart of the rechles and careles Christians. I heard and saw words and deeds of such force, that they might haue enforced (if I may vse such kinde of speach,) euen Almightie God himselfe, and incline him vnto mercy. I sawe many of those Holie penitents, which stood the whole night abrode in the aier, watching, and neuer so much as once mouing out of one place. And when sleepe seemed to ouercome them, they stroue, and reuiled them selues with verie iniurious wordes: and so by force they repelled the sleepe away fro^ their h^auy eies, because they would not yeeld vnto their bodies that little rest. Others I sawe standing with their eies fixed towardes Heauen, calling continually
 vnto Almightie God, with teares, and sighes for pardon and mercie. Others contrariewise saied with the Publican, that they were not worthie to lift vp their eyes towards Heauen,Luke. 18. verse. 13. neyther yet to speake vnto Almighty God. And after this sort they held their faces downe to the ground, offering their soules in silence vnto the mercy of God, with out speaking any one word at all, as men that had bin dumbe, full of feare and confusion. There were others cloathed in sacke, and haire-cloath, which were kneeling with their faces bowed downe to their knees, striking their foreheads ofte^times to the earth, with great sorrow, and bitternes of minde. Among these there were some, that had before them the very earth all wette, and bathed with teares. Others there were, which (because they wanted those teares) lamented verie grieuously. Many of them did (as the custome is ouer the graues of the dead) bewaile their owne soules, weeping and lamenting the fall and death of them. Others after the manner of Lyons roared and howled in the bottome of their heartes, yet repressing within them their sorrow and griefe: and sometimes (when they were not able to refraine anie more) they burst out sodainely into grieuous clamours, and dolorous lamentations. I saw certaine of them, who in their iudgements, deedes, and thoughts, were so far distracted from themselues, as if they had bin Images of stone: For by reason
 of their great pensiuenes, they were become in a ma^ner vnsensible of anie thing. And these had their soules, as it were drowned in the bottome of humilitie: and with the continuall fire of their heauines, had alreadie dried vpp the fountaines of their teares.
And alitle after in the saide Historie, this holy Father goeth forward, and saith in this wise: There mightest thou haue seen those Holie penitents, going in a malancholie maner, and loking downe to the earth: who haui^g already co^temned the thoughts of their flesh, mingled the bread which they did eat with ashes and their drinke with teares. There could not be heard among them anie other wordes, than these.

O wretch, that I am! Woe is me most miserable sinner. How iustlie, how iustlie, haue I deserued the wrath and anger of Almightie God. Pardon me, O Lord: Pardon me, O Lord. Manie of them had their tonges hanging out of their mouthes, like vnto wearied dogges, that were tired with ouermuch runing, and halfe dead, and dried vp with extreme thirst Others stood parching themselues at the Sun in the middest of sommer. And others, after a contrarie sort, suffered themselues to freese in the cold and open aier, euen in the middest of winter. Some of the^ tooke a litle water to refresh their tongue, not drinking thereof so much as was necessarie. And others likewise did eate a little bread, and the rest they
 cast from them, saying: that they were not worthy to eate the meate of men, sith they had done the deedes of beastes.


Now among such exercises, what place was there for laughing, or idle wordes, for anger, and malice? Where was there eyther Feasting, or banketting? Who was there, that tooke care how to delight and pamper the bodie with delicacie, and wantonnesse? Where was there so much as one sparckle of vaine glorie? Where were the delicate dishes and deuises of gluttonie? All their studie and care was to cry vnto our Lord both day, and night, and the sound of prayer and Meditation only was heard amongst them. There were some that stroke themselues very mightily vpon theyr breasts as if they had bin knocking at heauen gates,) and cryed out saying.

Open vnto vs, O thou mercifull Iudge, the gate which we haue through our iniquities shut so fast against vs: and other said.Psal. 79.4. Psal. 106.10.Shew thy face (O Lord) vnto vs, and wee shall be saued: an other saied. Shew thyselfe (O Lord) vnto these poore, and miserable sinners, which doe sitte in darkenesse, and in the shdadowe of death: an other saide.Luc. 1.78.Preuent vs (O Lord) speedilie with thy mercie: for we be sore empouerished. Psal. 78. verse. 78. Others said. Shall it happely please our Lorde to shew one daie his ioyfull countenance vnto vs? Or shall wee heare one daie that sweete
 voice, that saieth: vnto those that are imprisoned, Saluation:Esay. 49. verse. 9. and to those that be in darkenesse, receaue ye light.
They had death continually before their eyes, and speaking one to an other they sayed: How thinke yee brethren? What shall become of vs at that dreadfull houre? What shall our end be? Trow yee, that the sentence of our condemnation shalbe reuoked? Or shall our praiers perchance come vnto our Lords eares? And if they doe come, how shall they be receaued? What commoditie shall we haue by them? How much shall they pacifie him? For siih they proceed out of such vncleane lippes, it may be feared, that they shall finde small fauour in his sight. Who can tell, whether perhaps the holy Angels,Mat. 18. verse 10. Heb. 1.14.vnto whose custodie wee are commended, be at this present here about vs, or whether they be departed away from vs, by reason of the great stench of our sinnes? Some of them made answere vnto these demaundes, and sayed: But who knoweth,Ionas. 3.9. Quis scit, si conuertatur and ignoscat Deus, and reuertatur a furore irae suae, and non peribimus? Psa. 110.4. Psa. 144.5.(as those Penitent sinners of Niniuie saied,) whether our Lord will pardon vs, and whether he wil turne himselfe vnto vs, and not suffer vs to perish? Wherefore let vs now take good courage, and perseuere continually in crying vnto him, vntill the end of our liues: For our Lord is mercifull, and will be pacified with our perseuerance. Let vs runne my brethren, let vs runne I say, for it is very needfull, that we runne in all post
 hast, that we may speedily returne vnto the place, from whence we are fallen. Let vs runne alwaies towards that place, and let vs not in any wise pardon this our filthy flesh: but let vs continually be reuenged vpon it: yea, let vs crucifie our flesh, sith that our flesh hath first crucified vs.

Besides all this, what a meruailous thing was it: to behold the forme and euill treating of their owne bodies? They had faces like vnto dead men, and their eyes were sunke into their heades, by reason of ouer much weakenes. Their checkes were dried vp, and parched, and the haire of their eyelids falle^ away, through continuall weeping. Their knees were hardened like vnto Cammels knees, by continuall vse of payer. And their breasts were so galled with continuall knocking, that many of them auoided spittle mingled with blood. These blessed Penitents made their Petition vnto the Father of the Monasterie, (who was indeed a very Angell among men,) that he would fetter both theyr neckes, and handes in chaines, and shackle theyr feet with irons, and neuer to deliuer them from thence, vntill such time as they might be caried vnto their graues: of the which buriall also, they accounted themselues vnworthy.


But when their time of yeelding vp the Ghost approched neere, then was it more terrible to behold. They compassed the bedd of him that lay in dyinge rownd about, and demaunded of him, with
 vehement and earnest requestes, with mourning countenances, and pittifull wordes: saying. How doest thou brother? How feelest thou thy selfe? What saiest thou vnto vs? What hope haste thou? What shall become of thee? Haste thou happilie obteined thy long sute? Art thou ariued at the hauen of Saluation? Haste thou receaued no earnest pennie of thy securitie? Haste thou felt within thy heart any new light? Haste thou heard within thee any voice, that saied vnto thee: Thy sins are forgiuen thee?
Luc. 7.48. Mat. 9.22. Psal. 9.18. Mat. 22.14 Esa. 26.10.
Or: Thy Faith hath made thee safe? Or haste thou peraduenture heard anie other voice, that sayed vnto thee: Let the sinners descend downe into Hell, and all Nations that forget God? Or els: Binde him hand and foot, and cast him into the outward darkenesse. Or: Take away this wicked sinner, that he may neuer see the glorie of Almighty God? What answere makest thou, good brother vnto vs? Tell vs some thing we beseech thee: that wee may vnderstand by thee, what is reserued for vs: For thy sute is now come to an end. And what sentence thou shalt now receaue, shall neuer more be reuersed? but our cause dependeth still as yet, and expecteth for sentence. Vnto these demaundes certaine of them aunswered:
Psal. 23.
Blessed be our Lord, that hath not suffered vs to be cast into our enimies teeth. Others aunswered after a more dolesull sort. Miserable is that soule, that hath not fullie obserued his profession:
 For now shall he well vnderstand, what is prepared for him.


Now, when I had seene and heard all these thinges about mentioned, I was so wholly amazed and astonished within my selfe, that meruaile it was, that I fell not into a great extreame sadnesse, considering the negligence of my life past, and withall the slackenes of my pennance for my sinnes, being compared with the Penance of these Holie religious men.


But besides all this, what shall I say of theyr house, and lodging, in which they dwelled? For it was so foule and obscure, and so horrible and stincking withall, that certainely it was (as they tearmed it,) a very prison indeed: and such a one, as the only sight and forme thereof, was able of it selfe to baue taught a man pennance.
