The first of these defects is, when a man is ouermuch giuen vnto his outwarde affaires, and busines,1. Ouer-much giuen to outward exercises, and busines. and therefore is manie times depriued of inward visitations, and consolations: For a man findeth no thing of that without him, which ought to be sought for within him.
The second is,2. Ouermuch affabilitie and familiarity with many persons.Gal. 1.10. when hee will be ouermuch
 familiar, and affable with all men: whereof ensueth, that he shall not be able to rid himselfe of busines, and company, when it is requisite. And thus doth hee loose his time, and faileth oftentimes in his exercises, for that he will not faile the co^pany of men: whereby it commeth to passe, that the more hee studieth to please men, the lesse he pleaseth God.
The third is, when he is sometimes lesse humble towardes God,3. Presumptio^ and more bold than he ought to be, whereby hee looseth that spirituall bashfulnes which is requisite to be had towardes God: the which bashfulnes is the daughter of humility, and the mother of spirituall profit.
The fourth is, when sometimes he is too rash,4. Precipitation and rashnes in doing the affaires. Pro. 10.^. Qui festinus est pedibus, offe^det. and runneth headlong to his busines without any consideration, being rather lead by some sodaine passion of minde, tha^ by iudgment proceeding of reason, wherby hee looseth the peace, and tranquility of minde, through ouermuch feruour, and disordereth vvith all his owne affaires, through the ouermuch haste hee maketh in doing them: for it is written. Hee that hath light feet, is sure to stumble: wherefore in euerie thing it is needefull to haue alwaies a stayed iudgement, which is the
 faithfull friend, and companion of vvisedome.
The Fift is, that peraduenture sometimes he conceaueth a good opinion, and presumeth some what of himselfe, and of his owne vertues,5. Secret glory and presumption of himselfe, and of his owne vertues. Luk. 18.11 Summa. S. Thom. 2.2. quest. 161. art. 5. ad. 2. 6. albeit that hee himselfe doth not perceaue it: and so with the Pharisee secretly he contemneth others, and esteemeth himself much better: whereby he commeth to want the foundation of all vertues, which is humility.
The sixt is, when he is readie and inclined to iudge others, and to aggrauate,Rash iudgement.Note this well. and condemne theyr doings: wherby he commeth to wax cold in Charity: for the more he doth aggrauate other mens faults, the more he whetteth the knife, where-with he maketh war against Charity: for Charity ariseth partly of a good opinio^, which we conceaue of our neighbours.
The seauenth is, when hee hath as yet a great part of his loue set vpon transitorie things,7. Loue of transitory thinges. and therfore by good consequence, wanteth very much of the loue of God.
The eight is, when he is very slacke, and negligent in the exercise of praier,8. slackenes and negligence in the seruice of God. beginning it with slouthfulnes, prosecuting it with irkesomenes, and finishing it vvithout fruite: whereby it happeneth oftentimes,
 that he is depriued of our Lords visitations, and of the strength and comfort of deuotion.
The ninth is, when he is very slacke, and negligent, about the mortification,9. Slouthful and negligent in mortifying of himselfe. and subdueing of himselfe: whereby it commeth to passe, that hee can not liue vnto God, that liueth to himselfe: neyther can he be tra^sformed into God, who is not yet mortified in himsesfe.
10. Distraction of minde.The tenth is, when his minde is not closly recollected within himselfe: but runneth very much distracted and wandring out of himselfe: whereby it commeth, that he knoweth not so much of himselfe, as is needfull, and so vnderstandeth not how to despise himselfe, neyther yet how to haue an eye to himselfe, as it behoueth him.
11. Ouermuch loue of himselfe, and of his own will and appetite.The eleuenth is, when hee is far in loue with himselfe, and is a great follower of hys owne will and appetite: whereby it commeth that hee cannot denie himselfe, nor imbrace the Crosse of Christ, nor mortifie hys owne nature, and so hee cannot attaine vnto the perfection of the Euangelicall life.
The twelfe is, when he is inconstant, and mutable in such good purposes,12. Inconstancie in his good purposes. as hee determineth, breaking them off quickly vpon
 euery light occasion, that is offered vnto him. Whereby it commeth, that for lacke of perseuerance, (which is the only thing, that bringeth things to an end,Perseuerance bringeth things to an end.Psal. 26.14 Mat. 10.22 Mat. 24.13 Luke. 9.62. 2 Tim. 2.5 Heb. 3.14. Heb. 12.4. Apoc. 2.26. Apoc. 3.21. Apoc. 21.7.) he spendeth all his time in making euer new beginnings, and so encreaseth not, nor taketh any profit in Spirituall life. Such a one may vvell be compared vnto some Vines, vvhich beare Grapes all the yeare long, but neuer grow to be ripe.


The end of the first volume of the Memoriall of a Christian life.
DEO GRATIAS.
